JDBC 
  Java Database Connectivity 
Java Database Connectivity: It is an API (Application Programming Interface) in Java that allows 
Java applications to interact with databases. JDBC provides a standard way to connect to and execute 
queries on a database, enabling operations like retrieving, inserting, updating, and deleting data. 
Standard Steps followed for developing JDBC Application: 
To develop a JDBC (Java Database Connectivity) application, certain standard steps are followed to 
ensure the proper connection, interaction with the database, and closing of resources. Below are the 
standard steps for developing a JDBC application: 
1. Import JDBC Packages 
First, you need to import the required JDBC packages to work with JDBC in your Java program. 
Example: 
import java.sql.*; 
2. Register the JDBC Driver 
Before making a connection to the database, you need to load the JDBC driver class, which initiates 
the communication with the database. This step can be skipped for modern JDBC drivers (JDBC 4.0+), 
as they are auto-registered, but it’s good practice to explicitly register. 
Example: 
Class.forName("com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver"); 
  // For MySQL 
3. Establish a Connection 
You need to establish a connection to the database by using the DriverManager class. Provide the 
database URL, username, and password to connect. 
Example for MySQL: 
Connection conn = DriverManager.getConnection( 
    "jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/sakila", "username", "password"); 
4. Create a Statement 
Once the connection is established, you create a Statement or PreparedStatement object to send SQL 
queries to the database. 
Example: 
Using Statement: 
Statement stmt = conn.createStatement(); 
Using PreparedStatement (for parameterized queries): 
PreparedStatement pstmt = conn.prepareStatement("SELECT * FROM actor WHERE actor_id = ?"); 
5. Execute SQL Queries 
Depending on the type of SQL operation (e.g., SELECT, INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE), you use 
different methods to execute SQL queries: 
Example: 
For SELECT queries (which return a result set): 
ResultSet rs = stmt.executeQuery("SELECT * FROM actor"); 
For INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE, or DDL statements (which don't return a result set): 
int rowsAffected = stmt.executeUpdate("UPDATE actor SET first_name = 'Sai' WHERE actor_id = 4"); 
6. Process the Results 
If the query returns a ResultSet (as in a SELECT query), you need to process the results: 
Example: 
while (rs.next()) { 
    int actorId = rs.getInt("actor_id"); 
    String firstName = rs.getString("first_name"); 
    String lastName = rs.getString("last_name"); 
    System.out.println(actorId + " " + firstName + " " + lastName); 
} 
7. Close Resources: 
It is important to close the database resources after use to avoid memory leaks and ensure proper 
database management. Close the ResultSet, Statement, and Connection objects in the reverse order 
they were opened. 
Example: 
rs.close(); 
stmt.close(); 
conn.close(); 
Here is the scenario example of how JDBC works in the 
backend: as show in the below figure… 
Step1: 
1. Load and register the Driver 
A third party db vendor class which implements java.sql.Driver(I) is called as "Driver".This class Object we need to 
create and register it with JRE to set up JDBC 
environment to run jdbc applications. 
Note: 
public class com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver extends 
com.mysql.cj.jdbc.NonRegisteringDriver implements java.sql.Driver { 
public com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver() throws java.sql.SQLException; 
static {}; 
} 
In MySQL Jar, Driver class is implementing java.sql.Driver, so Driver class Objectshould be created and it should be 
registeredto set up the JDBC environment inside JRE. 
Step2: 
2. Establish the Connection b/w java application and database 
public static Connection getConnection(String url, String username,String password) throws SQLException; 
public static Connection getConnection(String url, Properties) throws SQLException; 
public static Connection getConnection(String url) throws SQLException; 
The below creates the Object of Connection interface. 
Connection connection = DriverManager.getConnection(url,username,password); 
| 
getConnection(url,username,password) created an object of class which implements Connection(I) that class object is 
collected by Connection(I).This feature in java refers to 
a. Abstraction(hiding internal services) 
b. polymorphism(making code run in 1:M forms) 
Can we create an Object for Interface? 
Answer. no 
Can we create an Object for a class which implements interface? 
Answer : yes 
Step3: 
3. Create a Statement Object 
public abstract Statement createStatement() throws SQLException; 
public abstract Statement createStatement(int,int) throws SQLException; 
public abstract Statement createStatement(int,int,int) throws SQLException; 
Statement statement = connection.createStatement(); 
Step4: 
4. Send and execute the Query 
Query 
From DB administrator perspective queries are classified into 5 types 
1. DDL (Create table,alter table,drop table,..) 
2. DML(Insert,update,delete) 
3. DQL(select) 
4. DCL(alter password,grant access) 
5. TCL(commit,rollback,savepoint) 
According to java developer perspective, we catergorise queires into 2 types 
a. Select Query 
b. NonSelect Query 
Methods for executing the Query are 
a. executeQuery() => for select query we use this method. 
b. executeUpdate() => for insert,update and delete query we use this method. 
c. execute() => for both select and non-select query we use this method 
public abstract ResultSet executeQuery(String sqlSelectQuery) throws SQLException; 
String sqlSelectQuery ="select sid,sname,sage,saddr from Student"; 
ResultSet resultSet = statement.executeQuery(sqlSelectQuery); 
5. Process the result from ResultSet 
public abstract boolean next() throws java.sql.SQLException; 
|=> To check whether next Record 
is available or not 
returns true if available 
otherwise returns false. 
System.out.println("SID\tSNAME\tSAGE\tSADDR"); 
while(resultSet.next()){ 
Integer id = resultSet.getInt(1); 
String name = resultSet.getString(2); 
Integer age = resultSet.getInt(3); 
String team = resultSet.getString(4); 
System.out.println(id+"\t"+name+"\t"+age+"\t"+team); 
} 
6. Close the Connection: 
rs.close(); 
stmt.close(); 
conn.close(); 
Table: 
Code Example… 
package com.JDBCD_MYSQLConnectivity; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.DriverManager; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.sql.Statement; 
import com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver; 
public class FirstJdbcCode { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws SQLException { 
  // Step:1 Load and Register the Driver... 
  Driver mySqldriver = new Driver(); // Creating driver object for mySqlDb 
  DriverManager.registerDriver(mySqldriver); 
  System.out.println("Driver Register Sucessfully....."); 
  // Step2: Estibilishing the connection between Java and the Data Base... 
  // JDBC Url Syntax :: <mainprotocol>:<subprotocol>:<subname> 
  String url = "jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testschema"; 
  String username = "****"; 
  String password = "****"; 
  Connection connection = DriverManager.getConnection(url, username, password); 
  System.out.println("Connection object is created...: " + connection); 
  System.out.println(); 
  System.out.println("Implements class name of connection is....." + 
connection.getClass().getName()); 
  // Step3: Create Statement.... 
  Statement statement = connection.createStatement(); 
  System.out.println("Object is Created for the Statement...."+statement); 
  //Step4: Execute the Query.... 
  String selectQuery ="select 
SID,StudentName,StudentCource,StudentAge,StudentHomeCity from testschema.students"; 
  // Stored in Result set... 
  ResultSet resultset =statement.executeQuery(selectQuery); 
  //Step5: Process the Results in the Resullt Set... 
  System.out.println("SID\t \tStudent_Name\t \tCource\t \tAge\t \tCity"); 
  System.out.println("------------------------------------------"); 
  while(resultset.next()) 
  { 
   Integer sid = resultset.getInt(1); 
   String name = resultset.getString(2).trim(); 
   String cource = resultset.getString(3).trim(); 
   Integer age = resultset.getInt(4); 
   String city = resultset.getString(5).trim(); 
   System.out.println(sid+"\t \t"+name+"\t \t"+cource+"\t \t"+age+"\t 
\t"+city); 
  } 
  //Step6 :Close the Connection... 
  connection.close(); 
  System.out.println("Connection Closed"); 
 } 
}

Connection Closed 
1. Load and register the Driver 
In earlier version of JDBC 3.X we were loading and registering the driver using the 
following approach 
Driver driver = new Driver(); 
DriverManager.registerDriver(driver); 
Alternate to this we can also load the driver as shown below 
Class.forName("com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver"); 
class Driver{ 
static{ 
Driver driver = new Driver(); 
DriverManager.registerDriver(driver); 
} 
Note: We say a class represents a Driver, iff the class has implemented an 
interface called "java.sql.Driver(I)". 
MySQL => Driver(c) implements Driver(I) 
Oracle => OracleDriver(c) implements Driver(I) 
Postgresql => PostgreSqlDriver(c) implements Driver(I) 
From JDBC4.X onwards loading and registering would happen automatically depending 
upon the jar added in the classpath 
location of the project. 
Note: 
1. JVM will search for the jar in the classpath 
2. It will open the jar,move to META-INF folder 
3. It will open services folder 
4. It will search for java.sql.Driver file 
5. Whatever value which is present inside Driver file that would be loaded 
automatically using 
Class.forName(value) 
The above feature of JDBC4.X is called as "AutoLoading". 
Writing Jdbc Code on Industry Standards: 
package com.JDBCD_MYSQLConnectivity; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.DriverManager; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.sql.Statement; 
public class SelectQuery { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws SQLException { 
  Connection connection = null; 
  Statement statement = null; 
  ResultSet resultset = null; 
  // Establishing the connection 
  String url = "jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testschema"; 
  String username = "****"; 
  String password = "***** "; 
  try { 
   connection = DriverManager.getConnection(url, username, password); 
   if (connection != null) { 
    // 3 Create Statement Object; 
    statement = connection.createStatement(); 
    if (statement != null) { 
     // pass the query 
     String query =  
"select SID,StudentName,StudentCource,StudentAge,StudentHomeCity from testschema.students"; 
     // Execute the query 
     resultset = statement.executeQuery(query); 
     System.out.println("SID\t \tStudent_Name\t \tCource\t \tAge\t 
\tCity"); 
     System.out.println("----------------------"); 
     while (resultset.next()) { 
      Integer sid = resultset.getInt(1); 
      String name = resultset.getString(2).trim(); 
      String cource = resultset.getString(3).trim(); 
      Integer age = resultset.getInt(4); 
      String city = resultset.getString(5).trim(); 
      System.out.println(sid + "\t \t" + name + "\t \t" + 
cource + "\t \t" + age + "\t \t" + city); 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (SQLException e) { 
   System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } finally { 
   if (resultset != null) { 
    resultset.close(); 
   } 
   if (statement != null) { 
    statement.close(); 
   } 
   if (connection != null) { 
    connection.close(); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
}

Example2: Inserting the Data into Table Input from the User… 
package com.JDBCD_MYSQLConnectivity; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.DriverManager; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.sql.Statement; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
class UserDetails { 
    private int sid; 
    private String sname; 
    private String crcname; 
    private int sage; 
    private String city; 
    public void userInfo() { 
        try (Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in)) { 
            System.out.println("Enter the User Details to add"); 
            System.out.print("Enter the SID: "); 
            sid = sc.nextInt(); 
            sc.nextLine();  // Consume newline left-over 
            System.out.print("Enter the Student Name: "); 
            sname = sc.nextLine(); 
            System.out.print("Enter the Course Name: "); 
            crcname = sc.nextLine(); 
            System.out.print("Enter the Age: "); 
            sage = sc.nextInt(); 
            sc.nextLine();  // Consume newline left-over 
            System.out.print("Enter the City Name: "); 
            city = sc.nextLine(); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } 
    } 
    // Getters for accessing user details if needed 
    public int getSid() { 
        return sid; 
    } 
    public String getStudentname() { 
        return sname; 
    } 
    public String getCourcename() { 
        return crcname; 
    } 
    public int getStudentage() { 
        return sage; 
    } 
    public String getCity() { 
        return city; 
    } 
} 
public class InsertQuery { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Connection connection = null; 
        Statement statement = null; 
        ResultSet resultSet = null; 
        // Database connection details 
        String url = "jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testschema"; 
        String username = "*****"; 
        String password = "******"; 
        UserDetails ud = new UserDetails(); 
        ud.userInfo(); 
  try { 
            // Establish the database connection 
            connection = DriverManager.getConnection(url, username, password); 
            if (connection != null) { 
                // Create a Statement object 
                statement = connection.createStatement(); 
                // Construct the insert query 
             //   To resolve the problem of the above approach we use a inbuilt class called"String". 
//                public static String format(String format, Object... args) { 
//                 return new Formatter().format(format, args).toString(); 
//                }  
//note: String use format specifier as '%s'....,int use format specifier as %d....,flaot use format 
specifier as %f 
//                "INSERT INTO testschema.students (SID, StudentName, StudentCource, StudentAge, 
StudentHomeCity) VALUES (" 
//                + ud.getSid() + ", '" + ud.getSname() + "', '" + ud.getCrcname() + "', " 
//                + ud.getSage() + ", '" + ud.getCity() + "')"; 
                String insertQuery = String.format("INSERT INTO testschema.students (SID, StudentName, 
StudentCource, StudentAge, StudentHomeCity) VALUES(%d,'%s','%s',%d,'%s')", 
ud.getSid(),ud.getStudentname(),ud.getCourcename(),ud.getStudentage(),ud.getCity()); 
                System.out.println(); 
                System.out.println("Query: " + insertQuery); 
                // Execute the insert query 
                int noOfRows = statement.executeUpdate(insertQuery); 
                System.out.println("No of Rows Affected: " + noOfRows); 
                // Query to retrieve all records 
                String query = "SELECT SID, StudentName, StudentCource, StudentAge, StudentHomeCity FROM 
testschema.students"; 
                // Execute the select query 
                resultSet = statement.executeQuery(query); 
                System.out.println("SID\tStudent_Name\tCourse\tAge\tCity"); 
                System.out.println("---------------------------------------------------------"); 
                // Print each record 
                while (resultSet.next()) { 
                    int sid = resultSet.getInt("SID"); 
                    String name = resultSet.getString("StudentName").trim(); 
                    String course = resultSet.getString("StudentCource").trim(); 
                    int age = resultSet.getInt("StudentAge"); 
                    String city = resultSet.getString("StudentHomeCity").trim();                   
      System.out.println(sid + "\t" + name + "\t" + course + "\t" + age + "\t" + city); 
                } 
            } 
        } catch (SQLException e) { 
            System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            // Close resources 
            try { 
                if (resultSet != null) resultSet.close(); 
                if (statement != null) statement.close(); 
                if (connection != null) connection.close(); 
            } catch (SQLException se) { 
                se.printStackTrace(); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

package com.JDBCD_MYSQLConnectivity; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.DriverManager; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.sql.Statement; 
public class UpdateQuery { 
 public static void main(String[] args) 
      throws SQLException { 
  Connection connection = null; 
  Statement statement = null; 
  ResultSet resultset = null; 
  // Establishing the connection 
  String url = "jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testschema"; 
  String username = "******"; 
  String password = "*******"; 
  try { 
   connection = DriverManager.getConnection(url, username, password); 
   if (connection != null) { 
    // 3 Create Statement Object; 
    statement = connection.createStatement(); 
    if (statement != null) { 
     // pass the query 
String updateQuery = "update testschema.students set StudentName = 'Roy',StudentCource 
='linux',StudentAge =33,StudentHomeCity='Wrl' where SID = 12"; 
     int noofRows = statement.executeUpdate(updateQuery); 
     System.out.println("No of rows effected....:: "+noofRows ); 
        System.out.println("After Update Table Info...."); 
String query = "select SID,StudentName,StudentCource,StudentAge,StudentHomeCity from 
testschema.students"; 
     // Execute the query 
     resultset = statement.executeQuery(query); 
     System.out.println("SID\t \tStudent_Name\t \tCource\t \tAge\t 
\tCity"); 
     System.out.println("---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------"); 
     while (resultset.next()) { 
      Integer sid = resultset.getInt(1); 
      String name = resultset.getString(2).trim(); 
      String cource = resultset.getString(3).trim(); 
      Integer age = resultset.getInt(4); 
      String city = resultset.getString(5).trim(); 
      System.out.println(sid + "\t \t" + name + "\t \t" + cource 
+ "\t \t" + age + "\t \t" + city); 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (SQLException e) { 
   System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } finally { 
   if (resultset != null) { 
    resultset.close(); 
   } 
   if (statement != null) { 
    statement.close(); 
   } 
   if (connection != null) { 
    connection.close(); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
}

package com.JDBCD_MYSQLConnectivity; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.DriverManager; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.sql.Statement; 
public class DelectQuery { 
 public static void main(String[] args)  
throws SQLException { 
  Connection connection = null; 
  Statement statement = null; 
  ResultSet resultset = null; 
  // Establishing the connection 
  String url = "jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testschema"; 
  String username = "****"; 
  String password = "****"; 
  try { 
   connection = DriverManager.getConnection(url, username, password); 
   if (connection != null) { 
    // 3 Create Statement Object; 
    statement = connection.createStatement(); 
    if (statement != null) { 
     // pass the query 
     String deleteQuery = "Delete from testschema.students where 
StudentName = ‘null’;"; 
     int noofRows = statement.executeUpdate(deleteQuery); 
     System.out.println("No of rows effected....:: "+noofRows ); 
        System.out.println("After Update Table Info...."); 
     String query = "select 
SID,StudentName,StudentCource,StudentAge,StudentHomeCity from testschema.students"; 
     // Execute the query 
     resultset = statement.executeQuery(query); 
     System.out.println("SID\tStudent_Name\t \tCource\t \tAge\tCity"); 
     System.out.println("-----------------------------------------------------------"); 
     while (resultset.next()) { 
      Integer sid = resultset.getInt(1); 
      String name = resultset.getString(2).trim(); 
      String cource = resultset.getString(3).trim(); 
      Integer age = resultset.getInt(4); 
      String city = resultset.getString(5).trim(); 
      System.out.println(sid + "\t" + name + "\t \t" + cource + 
"\t \t" + age + "\t" + city); 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (SQLException e) { 
   System.out.println(e.getMessage()); 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } finally { 
   if (resultset != null) { 
    resultset.close(); 
   } 
   if (statement != null) { 
    statement.close(); 
   } 
   if (connection != null) { 
    connection.close(); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
}

Problem with statement Object: 
Statement stmt = con.createStatement(); 
ResultSet rs = stmt.exectueQuery("select * from student"); 
If we use Statement Object, same query will be compiled every time and the query should be executed everytime,this 
would create performance problems. 
eg: IRCTC App(select query), BMS APP(select query) 
To Overcome This 
Prepare Statement is 
Introduced 
Prepare Statement: 
In JDBC, a PreparedStatement is an interface used to execute parameterized SQL queries. It offers better performance and 
security compared to regular Statement objects, especially when working with repeated or complex queries. 
Key Benefits of PreparedStatement 
 Pre-compilation: The query is compiled only once, even if it's executed multiple times. This improves performance. 
 Parameterized Queries: Allows the use of placeholders (?) for parameters, preventing SQL injection. 
 Automatic Escaping: JDBC handles special characters in the parameter values, making it safer and easier to work with 
user input. 
To resolve the above problem don't use Statement Object, use "PreparedStatement(Pre-CompiledStatement)".In case of PreparedStatement, the query 
will be compiled only once eveythough we are executing it mulitple time with change or no change in inputs. This would overall increase the 
performance.signature 
public PreparedStatement prepareStatement(String sqlQuery) throws SQLException 
 //Establish the connection 
 Connection con = DriverManger.getConnection(url,username,password); 
 //Creating a precompiled query which is used at the runtime to execute with the 
 value 
 String sqlSelectQuery = "select sid,sname,sage,saddr from student where sid = ?"; 
 PreparedStatemetn pstmt = con.prepareStatement(sqlSelectQuery); 
At this line, sqlquery will be sent to database, DatabaseEngine will compile the query and stores in database. 
That precompiled query will be sent to the java application in the form of 
 "PreparedStatement" Object. 
 Hence PreparedStatement Object is called "PreCompiledQuery" object. 
 // Execute the PreCompiledQuery by setting the inputs 
 Integer sid = 10; 
 pstmt.setInt(1,sid); 
 ResultSet resultSet = pstmt.executeQuery(); 
 //process the resultSet 
 pstmt.setInt(1,100); 
 ResultSet resultSet = pstmt.executeQuery(); 
Whenever we execute methods, databasengine will not compile query once again and it 
will directly execute that query, 
so that overall performance will be improved 
Note: 
String sqlQuery= insert into 
student(`sid`,`sname`,`sage`,`saddres`) 
values(?,?,?,?); 
PreparedStatement pstmt = 
con.prepareStatement(sqlQuery); 
pstmt.setInt(1,10); 
pstmt.setString(2,"sachin"); 
pstmt.setInt(3,45); 
pstmt.setString(4,"MI"); 
int rowCount = pstmt.executeUpdate(); 
package PrepareStatement; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.PreparedStatement; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
public class InsertQueyPrepareStatement { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws SQLException { 
   JdbcMysqlConnection  jdbcConnection = new JdbcMysqlConnection(); 
   Connection connection = null; 
   PreparedStatement prepareStatement = null; 
   String insertQuery =""; 
   Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
  try { 
     jdbcConnection.setFilters(sc); 
     jdbcConnection.userInfo(sc); 
     connection =jdbcConnection.getJdbcMysqlConnection(); 
     if(connection!=null) 
     { 
      insertQuery = "INSERT INTO testschema.students (StudentName, 
StudentCourse, StudentAge, StudentHomeCity) VALUES(?,?,?,?)"; 
      prepareStatement = connection.prepareStatement(insertQuery); 
      if(prepareStatement!=null && (!insertQuery.isEmpty())) 
      { 
      prepareStatement.setString(1, jdbcConnection.getStudentName()); 
      prepareStatement.setString(2, jdbcConnection.getCourseName()); 
      prepareStatement.setInt(3, jdbcConnection.getStudentAge()); 
      prepareStatement.setString(4, jdbcConnection.getCity()); 
      int noofrowseffected = prepareStatement.executeUpdate(); 
      System.out.println("No of Rows Effected : "+noofrowseffected); 
      }    
     } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  finally { 
   jdbcConnection.closeConnection(null, prepareStatement, connection); 
   if(sc!=null) 
   { 
    sc.close(); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
}

The JdbcMysqlConnection class can be called a Data Access Object (DAO). In Java, a DAO class is responsible for interacting 
with the database and performing operations such as creating, reading, updating, and deleting data. DAOs handle database 
connections, queries, and transactions, making them ideal for organizing database-related code. 
package PrepareStatement; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.DriverManager; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.sql.Statement; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
public class JdbcMysqlConnection { 
    private int studentId; 
    private String studentName; 
    private String courseName; 
    private int studentAge; 
    private String nativeCity; 
    // Renamed boolean flags for clarity 
    private boolean isSidFilterEnabled = false; 
    private boolean isSnameFilterEnabled = false; 
    private boolean isCourseFilterEnabled = false; 
    private boolean isSageFilterEnabled = false; 
    private boolean isCityFilterEnabled = false; 
    // Database connection details 
    private static final String URL = "jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testschema"; 
    private static final String USERNAME = "*****"; 
    private static final String PASSWORD = "*****"; 
    public Connection getJdbcMysqlConnection() { 
        Connection connection = null; 
        try { 
            connection = DriverManager.getConnection(URL, USERNAME, PASSWORD); 
            if (connection != null) { 
                System.out.println("***** Connected Successfully *****"); 
            } 
        } catch (SQLException e) { 
            System.err.println("SQL Exception: " + e.getMessage()); 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            System.err.println("General Exception: " + e.getMessage()); 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } 
        return connection; 
    } 
    public void closeConnection(ResultSet resultSet, Statement statement, Connection 
connection) { 
        try { 
            if (resultSet != null) { 
                resultSet.close(); 
            } 
            if (statement != null) { 
                statement.close(); 
            } 
            if (connection != null) { 
                connection.close(); 
                System.out.println("**** Connection closed Successfully *****"); 
            } 
        } catch (SQLException e) { 
            System.err.println("SQL Exception: " + e.getMessage()); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            System.err.println("General Exception: " + e.getMessage()); 
        } 
    } 
    public void userInfo(Scanner sc) { 
        System.out.println("<------- Enter the User Details -------->"); 
        try { 
            if (isSidFilterEnabled) { 
                System.out.print("Enter the SID: "); 
                studentId = sc.nextInt(); 
                sc.nextLine(); // Consume newline left-over 
            } 
            if (isSnameFilterEnabled) { 
                System.out.print("Enter the Student Name: "); 
                studentName = sc.nextLine(); 
            } 
            if (isCourseFilterEnabled) { 
                System.out.print("Enter the Course Name: "); 
                courseName = sc.nextLine(); 
            } 
            if (isSageFilterEnabled) { 
                System.out.print("Enter the Age: "); 
                studentAge = sc.nextInt(); 
                sc.nextLine(); // Consume newline left-over 
            } 
            if (isCityFilterEnabled) { 
                System.out.print("Enter the City Name: "); 
                nativeCity = sc.nextLine(); 
            } 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            System.err.println("Error reading user info: " + e.getMessage()); 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } 
    } 
    public void setFilters(Scanner scanner) { 
        System.out.println("Set filters for querying the students table. Enter 'yes' --Key-> Y/y Else --->'No' --Key-> 
N/n to filter by each attribute."); 
        try { 
            System.out.print("Filter by SID? (yes/no): "); 
            isSidFilterEnabled = scanner.nextLine().equalsIgnoreCase("y"); 
            System.out.print("Filter by Student Name? (yes/no): "); 
            isSnameFilterEnabled = scanner.nextLine().equalsIgnoreCase("y"); 
            System.out.print("Filter by Course? (yes/no): "); 
            isCourseFilterEnabled = scanner.nextLine().equalsIgnoreCase("y"); 
            System.out.print("Filter by Student Age? (yes/no): "); 
            isSageFilterEnabled = scanner.nextLine().equalsIgnoreCase("y"); 
            System.out.print("Filter by City? (yes/no): "); 
            isCityFilterEnabled = scanner.nextLine().equalsIgnoreCase("y"); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            System.err.println("Error setting filters: " + e.getMessage()); 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } 
    } 
    // Getter methods for filter flags 
    public boolean isSidFilterEnabled() { 
        return isSidFilterEnabled; 
    } 
    public boolean isSnameFilterEnabled() { 
        return isSnameFilterEnabled; 
    } 
    public boolean isCourseFilterEnabled() { 
        return isCourseFilterEnabled; 
    } 
    public boolean isSageFilterEnabled() { 
        return isSageFilterEnabled; 
    } 
    public boolean isCityFilterEnabled() { 
        return isCityFilterEnabled; 
    } 
    // Getters for student attributes 
    public int getSid() { 
        return studentId; 
    } 
    public String getStudentName() { 
        return studentName; 
    } 
    public String getCourseName() { 
        return courseName; 
    } 
    public int getStudentAge() { 
        return studentAge; 
    } 
    public String getCity() { 
        return nativeCity; 
    } 
} 
Select Query Code By Using Scanner Class based on User Input 
package PrepareStatement; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.PreparedStatement; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
public class SelectQueryByPrepareStatement { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        JdbcMysqlConnection jdbcConnection = new JdbcMysqlConnection(); 
        Connection connection = null; 
        PreparedStatement preparedStatement = null; 
        ResultSet resultSet = null; 
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
        try { 
            connection = jdbcConnection.getJdbcMysqlConnection(); 
            if (connection != null) { 
                // Call the userInfo to gather filters and user input 
                jdbcConnection.setFilters(sc); 
                jdbcConnection.userInfo(sc); 
                // Dynamically build SQL query based on selected filters 
                StringBuilder queryBuilder = new StringBuilder("SELECT * FROM testschema.students WHERE 1=1"); 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSidFilterEnabled()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND SID = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSnameFilterEnabled()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentName = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCourseFilterEnabled()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentCourse = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSageFilterEnabled()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentAge = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCityFilterEnabled()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentHomeCity = ?"); 
                } 
                String selectQuery = queryBuilder.toString(); 
                System.out.println("Query  :: " + selectQuery); 
                System.out.println(); 
                preparedStatement = connection.prepareStatement(selectQuery); 
                int paramIndex = 1; 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSidFilterEnabled()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setInt(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getSid()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSnameFilterEnabled()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getStudentName().trim()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCourseFilterEnabled()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getCourseName().trim()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSageFilterEnabled()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setInt(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getStudentAge()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCityFilterEnabled()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getCity().trim()); 
                } 
                resultSet = preparedStatement.executeQuery(); 
                // Display the results 
                if (!resultSet.isBeforeFirst()) { // Check if results exist 
                    StringBuilder criteriaMessage = new StringBuilder("No records found matching your criteria. Details provided:\n"); 
                    // Append details for each filter used in the query 
                    if (jdbcConnection.isSidFilterEnabled()) { 
                        criteriaMessage.append("SID: ").append(jdbcConnection.getSid()).append(" \t"); 
                    } 
                    if (jdbcConnection.isSnameFilterEnabled()) { 
                        criteriaMessage.append("Student Name: ").append(jdbcConnection.getStudentName()).append(" \t"); 
                    } 
                    if (jdbcConnection.isCourseFilterEnabled()) { 
                        criteriaMessage.append("Course Name: ").append(jdbcConnection.getCourseName()).append(" \t"); 
                    } 
                    if (jdbcConnection.isSageFilterEnabled()) { 
                        criteriaMessage.append("Student Age: ").append(jdbcConnection.getStudentAge()).append(" \t"); 
                    } 
                    if (jdbcConnection.isCityFilterEnabled()) { 
                        criteriaMessage.append("City: ").append(jdbcConnection.getCity()).append(" \t"); 
                    } 
                    System.out.println(criteriaMessage.toString()); 
                } else { 
                    while (resultSet.next()) { 
                        Integer studentId = resultSet.getInt("SID"); 
                        String name = resultSet.getString("StudentName").replaceAll("\\s+", " ").trim(); 
                        String courseValue = resultSet.getString("StudentCourse").replaceAll("\\s+", " ").trim(); 
                        Integer age = resultSet.getInt("StudentAge"); 
                        String nativeCity = resultSet.getString("StudentHomeCity").replaceAll("\\s+", " ").trim(); 
                        System.out.println("Student Id :: " + studentId + " ; StudentName :: " + name + "; Course Name :: " + 
courseValue + " ; Student Age :: " + age + "; Home City :: " + nativeCity); 
                    } 
                } 
            } 
        } catch (SQLException e) { 
            System.err.println("Database error: " + e.getMessage()); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            jdbcConnection.closeConnection(resultSet, preparedStatement, connection); 
            if (sc != null) { 
                sc.close(); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

Update Query Code By Using Scanner Class based on User Input 
 package PrepareStatement; 
import java.sql.*; 
public class UpdateQueryPrepareStaement { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        JdbcMysqlConnection jdbcConnection = new JdbcMysqlConnection(); 
        Connection connection = null; 
        PreparedStatement preparedStatement = null; 
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
        try { 
            connection = jdbcConnection.getJdbcMysqlConnection(); 
            if (connection != null) { 
                jdbcConnection.setFilters(sc); // Set filters for selecting the records to update 
                System.out.println("<----Enter the User Old Values To Update ---->"); 
                jdbcConnection.userInfo(sc); 
                System.out.println("Enter the new details for updating (leave blank to skip):"); 
                System.out.print("New Student Name: ");                // Collect new values to update 
                String newName = sc.nextLine().trim(); 
                System.out.print("New Course Name: "); 
                String newCourse = sc.nextLine().trim(); 
                System.out.print("New Age: "); 
                String ageInput = sc.nextLine().trim(); 
                Integer newAge = ageInput.isEmpty() ? null : Integer.parseInt(ageInput); 
                System.out.print("New Home City: "); 
                String newCity = sc.nextLine().trim(); 
                // Building the SQL Update Query 
                StringBuilder queryBuilder = new StringBuilder("UPDATE testschema.students SET "); 
                boolean hasUpdates = false; 
                // Building SET clause 
                if (!newName.isEmpty()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append("StudentName = ?"); 
                    hasUpdates = true; 
                } 
                if (!newCourse.isEmpty()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(hasUpdates ? ", StudentCourse = ?" : "StudentCourse = ?"); 
                    hasUpdates = true; 
                } 
                if (newAge != null) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(hasUpdates ? ", StudentAge = ?" : "StudentAge = ?"); 
                    hasUpdates = true; 
                } 
                if (!newCity.isEmpty()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(hasUpdates ? ", StudentHomeCity = ?" : "StudentHomeCity = ?"); 
                } 
                queryBuilder.append(" WHERE 1=1");// Adding filters to target specific rows 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSidFilterEnabled() && jdbcConnection.getSid() != 0) { // Add only non-null or non-empty filters 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND SID = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSnameFilterEnabled() && jdbcConnection.getStudentName() != null && 
!jdbcConnection.getStudentName().isEmpty()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentName = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCourseFilterEnabled() && jdbcConnection.getCourseName() != null && 
!jdbcConnection.getCourseName().isEmpty()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentCourse = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSageFilterEnabled() && jdbcConnection.getStudentAge() != 0) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentAge = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCityFilterEnabled() && jdbcConnection.getCity() != null && !jdbcConnection.getCity().isEmpty()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentHomeCity = ?"); 
                } 
                String updateQuery = queryBuilder.toString(); 
                System.out.println("Generated Update Query: " + updateQuery); 
                preparedStatement = connection.prepareStatement(updateQuery); 
                int paramIndex = 1;                
                if (!newName.isEmpty()) { // Setting new values to update 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, newName); 
                } 
                if (!newCourse.isEmpty()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, newCourse); 
                } 
                if (newAge != null) { 
                    preparedStatement.setInt(paramIndex++, newAge); 
                } 
                if (!newCity.isEmpty()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, newCity); 
                } 
                // Setting filter conditions for the WHERE clause 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSidFilterEnabled() && jdbcConnection.getSid() != null) { 
                    preparedStatement.setInt(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getSid()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSnameFilterEnabled() && jdbcConnection.getStudentName() != null && 
!jdbcConnection.getStudentName().isEmpty()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getStudentName().trim()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCourseFilterEnabled() && jdbcConnection.getCourseName() != null && 
!jdbcConnection.getCourseName().isEmpty()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getCourseName().trim()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSageFilterEnabled() && jdbcConnection.getStudentAge() != null) { 
                    preparedStatement.setInt(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getStudentAge()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCityFilterEnabled() && jdbcConnection.getCity() != null && !jdbcConnection.getCity().isEmpty()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getCity().trim()); 
                } 
                int rowsUpdated = preparedStatement.executeUpdate();// Execute the update and display the results 
                System.out.println(rowsUpdated + " row(s) updated."); 
            } 
        } catch (SQLException e) { 
            System.err.println("Database error: " + e.getMessage()); 
        } finally { 
            jdbcConnection.closeConnection(null, preparedStatement, connection); 
            sc.close(); 
        } 
    } 
}

Delete Query Code By Using Scanner Class based on User Input 
package PrepareStatement; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.PreparedStatement; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
public class DeleteQueryPrepareStatement { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        JdbcMysqlConnection jdbcConnection = new JdbcMysqlConnection(); 
        Connection connection = null; 
        PreparedStatement preparedStatement = null; 
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
        try { 
            connection = jdbcConnection.getJdbcMysqlConnection(); 
            if (connection != null) { 
                // Set filters for selecting the records to delete 
                jdbcConnection.setFilters(sc); 
                System.out.println("Enter the User Details to Delete ....."); 
                jdbcConnection.userInfo(sc); 
                // Building the SQL Delete Query based on filters 
                StringBuilder queryBuilder = new StringBuilder("DELETE FROM testschema.students 
WHERE 1=1"); 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSidFilterEnabled()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND SID = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSnameFilterEnabled()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentName = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCourseFilterEnabled()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentCourse = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSageFilterEnabled()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentAge = ?"); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCityFilterEnabled()) { 
                    queryBuilder.append(" AND StudentHomeCity = ?"); 
                } 
                String deleteQuery = queryBuilder.toString(); 
                System.out.println("Generated Delete Query: " + deleteQuery); 
                preparedStatement = connection.prepareStatement(deleteQuery); 
                int paramIndex = 1; 
                // Setting filter conditions for the WHERE clause 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSidFilterEnabled()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setInt(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getSid()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSnameFilterEnabled()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, 
jdbcConnection.getStudentName().trim()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCourseFilterEnabled()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, 
jdbcConnection.getCourseName().trim()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isSageFilterEnabled()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setInt(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getStudentAge()); 
                } 
                if (jdbcConnection.isCityFilterEnabled()) { 
                    preparedStatement.setString(paramIndex++, jdbcConnection.getCity().trim()); 
                } 
                // Execute the delete and display the results 
                int rowsDeleted = preparedStatement.executeUpdate(); 
                System.out.println(rowsDeleted + " row(s) deleted."); 
            } 
        } catch (SQLException e) { 
            System.err.println("Database error: " + e.getMessage()); 
        } finally { 
            jdbcConnection.closeConnection(null, preparedStatement, connection); 
            sc.close(); 
        } 
    } 
}

SQL Injection is a type of security vulnerability that occurs when an attacker can insert or manipulate 
SQL queries within an application's input fields. This vulnerability allows attackers to interfere with an 
application's database queries, potentially leading to unauthorized access, data modification, or even 
complete compromise of the database. 
How SQL Injection Works 
SQL Injection typically happens when an application does not properly sanitize user inputs that are used 
in SQL queries. For example: 
User Input Directly in Queries: Consider a basic SQL query that retrieves a user record based on a username 
and password entered in a login form: 
java 
Code Example :- 
String query = "SELECT * FROM users WHERE username = '" + userInput + "' AND password = '" + 
passwordInput + "'"; 
Malicious Input: If an attacker enters something like "admin' --" as userInput, the query would become: 
sql 
Code Example :- 
SELECT * FROM users WHERE username = 'admin' --' AND password = '' 
The -- comment sequence will ignore everything after admin, effectively making the query check only for 
the username and bypassing the password condition. 
Potential Impact: As a result, the attacker could gain access to the account without knowing the password 
or, in more extreme cases, could execute commands to view, alter, or delete data across the database. 
SQLInjection 
========== 
Users username upwd sachin Tendulkar virat kohli 
eg: 
select count(*) from users where username ='"+uname+"'" and upwd =' 
"+upwd+"'"; 
username = 'sachin' 
password = 'tendulkar' 
Query nature 
select count(*) from users where username ='sachin' and upwd =' tendulkar' "; 
validation is succesful and given the authentication 
eg: 
select count(*) from users where username ='"+uname+"'" and upwd =' 
"+upwd+"'"; 
username = 'sachin'--  password = 'tendulkar' 
Query nature 
select count(*) from users where username ='sachin'-- and upwd ='tendulkar'"; 
validation is succesfull and given the authentication 
Note: 
1. -- Single line sql comment 
2. /*Multiline sql comment*/ 
If we use Statement Object to send the Query, then the problem of 
SQLInjection will 
happen. 
eg: Statement stmt = con.createStatement(); 
String query = "select count(*) from users where username ='"+uname+"'" and 
upwd "+upwd+"'"; 
ResultSet resultSet =stmt.executeQuery(query); 
DB: select count(*) from users where username ='"+sachin'-- "; 
count(*) = 1 (validation is succesfull give 
authentication) 
if we use PreparedStatement Object to send the Query, then the 
problem of 
SQLInjection will not happen. 
eg: String query = "select count(*) from users where username =? 
and upwd 
=?"; 
PreparedStatement pstmt = con.prepareStatement(query); 
pstmt.setString(1,"sachin'--"); 
pstmt.setString(2,"tendulkar"); 
ResultSet resultSet =pstmt.executeQuery(); 
for compilation using PreparedStatement 
DB: select count(*) from users where username =? and upwd =?; 
select count(*) from users where username ='sachin'--' and upwd 
='tendulkar'; 
count(*) => 0 (validation not succesfull so no 
authentication) 
Note: In real time database used in production envrionment is 
"Oracle", only during 
development phase we 
use "MySQL" database. 
In MySQLDatabase, we can't perform "SQLInjection" through 
comments,it 
happens only in "OracleDatabase". 
So By Using Prepare Statement Instead of Satement That Would 
Be Helpful for both performace Wise and Security Wise…! 
Handling date values for database operations requires careful attention to both the format of the date and the database 
configuration. Here’s a general guide to handling Date objects in Java for database operations: 
1. Java Date Handling 
In Java, date and time handling typically involves classes such as java.util.Date, java.sql.Date, and the newer 
java.time.LocalDate or java.time.LocalDateTime (from Java 8+). 
For database operations, java.sql.Date, java.sql.Timestamp, and java.time classes (for newer databases) are commonly used. 
* Sometimes as the part of programing requirement,we have to insert and retrieve Date like DOB,DOJ,DOM,DOP...wrt 
database. 
* It is not recommended to maintain date values in the form of String,b'z comparisons will become difficult. 
In Java we have two Date classes 
1. java.util.Date 
2. java.sql.Date 
* java.sql.Date is the child class of java.util.Date. 
* java.sql.Date is specially designed class for handling Date values wrt database. Otherthan database operations,if we want to 
represent Date in our java program then we should go for java.util.Date. 
* java.util.Date can represent both Date and Time where as java.sql.Date represents only Date but not time. 
Differences between java.util.Date and java.sql.Date java.util.Date 
1) It is general Utility Class to handle Dates in our Java Program. 
2) It represents both Data and Time. 
java.sql.Date 
1) It is specially designed Class to handle Datesw.r.t DB Operations. 
2) It represents only Date but not Time. 
Note: 
* In sql package Time class is availble to represent Time values 
* In sql package TimeStamp class is available to represent both Date and Time. 
* Inserting Date Values into Database: 
Various databases follow various styles to represent Date. 
Eg: 
Oracle: dd-MMM-yy eg: 28-May-90 
MySQL : yyyy-mm-dd eg: 1990-05-28 
java.sql.Date * information is stored as "yyyy-mm-dd" 
* If we use simple Statement object to insert Date values then we should provide Date value in the database supported 
format,which is difficult to the programmer. 
* If we use PreparedStatement,then we are not required to worry about database supported form, 
just we have to call pst.setDate (2, java.sql.Date); 
This method internally converts date value into the database supported format. Hence it is highly recommended to use 
PreparedStatement to insert Date values into database. 
package SqlDate; 
import java.sql.Date; 
import java.sql.Timestamp; 
import java.text.ParseException; 
import java.text.SimpleDateFormat; 
public class SqlDateprgm { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  java.sql.Date  sqlDate = null; 
  Timestamp sqlTimestamp = null; 
  String dojInput = "26-07-2024"; 
  if (dojInput != null && !dojInput.trim().isEmpty()) { 
   try { 
    SimpleDateFormat sdf = new SimpleDateFormat("dd-mm-yyyy"); 
    java.util.Date utilDate = sdf.parse(dojInput.trim()); 
    sqlDate = new java.sql.Date(utilDate.getTime()); 
    System.out.println("Date : " + sqlDate); 
    sqlTimestamp = new Timestamp(utilDate.getTime()); 
    System.out.println("Timestamp : " + sqlTimestamp); 
    SimpleDateFormat sdf2 = new SimpleDateFormat("mm-dd-yyyy"); 
    String updateDate = sdf2.format(sqlDate); 
    System.out.println("Updated Date : "+updateDate); 
   } catch (ParseException e) { 
    System.out.println("Error: Date format should be dd-MM-yyyy."); 
    return; 
   } 
  } 
 } 
} 
Code Out Put: 
Date : 2024-01-26 
Timestamp : 2024-01-26 00:07:00.0 
Updated Date : 07-26-2024 
BLOB (Binary Large Object) and CLOB (Character Large Object) operations: 
Sometimes as the part of programming requirement,we have to insert and retrieve large files like images,video 
files,audio files,resume etc wrt database. 
Eg:upload image in matrinomial web sites 
upload resume in job related web sites To store and retrieve large information we should go for Large 
Objects(LOBs). 
There are 2 types of Large Objects. 
1. Binary Large Object (BLOB) 
2. Character Large Object (CLOB) 
1) Binary Large Object (BLOB) 
A BLOB is a collection of binary data stored as a single entity in the database. 
BLOB type objects can be images,video files,audio files etc.. 
BLOB datatype can store maximum of "4GB" binary data. 
eg: sachin.jpg 
2) CLOB (Character Large Objects): 
A CLOB is a collection of Character data stored as a single entity in the database. 
CLOB can be used to store large text documents(may plain text or xml documents) 
CLOB Type can store maximum of 4GB data. 
eg: resume.txt 
Blob Insert Example Code: 
package BlobAndClobApp; 
import java.io.File; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.FileNotFoundException; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.PreparedStatement; 
import PrepareStatement.JdbcMysqlConnection; 
public class BlobInsert { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Connection connection = null; 
  PreparedStatement prepareStatement = null; 
  JdbcMysqlConnection jdbcConnection = new JdbcMysqlConnection(); 
  try { 
   connection = jdbcConnection.getJdbcMysqlConnection(); 
   String inserQuery = "INSERT INTO testschema.studentidientity (SName,Simage) 
Values(?,?)"; 
   if(connection!=null) 
   { 
    prepareStatement  = connection.prepareStatement(inserQuery); 
    if(prepareStatement!=null) 
    { 
     // Setting the first index to String 
     prepareStatement.setString(1,"Rolex"); 
     // Image files is reaching to java application 
     File imgfile = new 
File("C:\\Users\\HP\\Pictures\\Screenshots\\Screenshot 2023-04-30 152229.png"); 
     FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream(imgfile); 
     // setting the input information from java and sending the data to 
database 
     prepareStatement.setBlob(2,fis); 
     System.out.println("Inserting image from :: " + 
imgfile.getAbsolutePath()); 
     // Executing the Query to get the result  
     int noofRows = prepareStatement.executeUpdate(); 
     if (noofRows == 1) { 
      System.out.println("record inserted succesfully..."); 
     } else { 
      System.out.println("No records inserted....."); 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (FileNotFoundException e) { 
   // hanlding logic of exception related to FileOperation 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   // hanlding logic of exception related to common problem 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  }finally { 
   jdbcConnection.closeConnection(null, prepareStatement, connection); 
  } 
 } 
}

package BlobAndClobApp; 
import java.io.File; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.FileNotFoundException; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.PreparedStatement;

import PrepareStatement.JdbcMysqlConnection; 
public class BlobUpdate { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Connection  connection = null; 
  PreparedStatement preparedStatement =null; 
  JdbcMysqlConnection jdbcConnection = new JdbcMysqlConnection(); 
  try { 
   connection = jdbcConnection.getJdbcMysqlConnection(); 
   String updateQuery = "update testschema.studentidientity set Simage 
=? where Sid = ?"; 
   if(connection!=null) 
   { 
    preparedStatement = connection.prepareStatement(updateQuery); 
    if(preparedStatement!=null) 
    { 
     File imageFile = new 
File("C:\\Users\\HP\\Pictures\\Screenshots\\Screenshot 2023-05-01 211620.png"); 
     FileInputStream fos = new FileInputStream(imageFile); 
     preparedStatement.setBlob(1, fos); 
     preparedStatement.setInt(2, 1); 
     int effetedRows = preparedStatement.executeUpdate(); 
     System.out.println("No of Rows Effected :: 
"+effetedRows);    
    } 
   } 
  } 
  catch (FileNotFoundException | SQLException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  finally { 
   jdbcConnection.closeConnection(null, preparedStatement, connection); 
  } 
 } 
}

package BlobAndClobApp; 
import java.io.File; 
import java.io.FileNotFoundException; 
import java.io.FileOutputStream; 
import java.io.InputStream; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.PreparedStatement; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import org.apache.commons.io.IOUtils; 
import PrepareStatement.JdbcMysqlConnection; 
public class RectriveBlobData { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Connection connection = null; 
  PreparedStatement prepareStatement = null; 
  ResultSet resultSet =null; 
  JdbcMysqlConnection jdbcConnection = new JdbcMysqlConnection(); 
  try { 
   connection = jdbcConnection.getJdbcMysqlConnection(); 
   String selectQuery = "Select Sid,SName,Simage from testschema.studentidientity 
where Simage is not null"; 
   if(connection!=null) 
   { 
    prepareStatement  = connection.prepareStatement(selectQuery); 
    if(prepareStatement!=null)   
    { 
     resultSet = prepareStatement.executeQuery();           
     if(resultSet!=null) 
     { 
      int counter =1; 
      while(resultSet.next()) 
      { 
       Integer sid = resultSet.getInt(1); 
       String name = resultSet.getString(2); 
       // fetching the image and keeping it in harddisk(just 
like downloading) 
       InputStream ins = resultSet.getBinaryStream(3); 
      // int i = ins.read(); 
       File file = new 
File("D:\\SQL\\SqlBlob\\Db_Dowload_image_"+counter+".png"); 
       FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream(file); 
     //byte buffer[] = new byte[2048]; ||    while(i!=-1){ 
     //while(ins.read(buffer)>0)       || fos.write(i); 
     //{          || i=ins.read(); 
     //  fos.write(buffer);           ||   }fos.flush(); 
     //}          || 
          IOUtils.copy(ins, fos); 
       counter++; 
       System.out.println(sid+" \t "+name); 
       System.out.println("File is saved to the location:: " 
+file.getAbsolutePath()); 
      } 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  }catch (SQLException|FileNotFoundException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  catch (Exception e) { 
   // hanlding logic of exception related to common problem 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  }finally { 
   jdbcConnection.closeConnection(null, prepareStatement, connection); 
  } 
 } 
}

package BlobAndClobApp; 
import java.io.File; 
import java.io.FileNotFoundException; 
import java.io.PrintWriter; 
import java.io.Reader; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.PreparedStatement; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import org.apache.commons.io.IOUtils; 
import PrepareStatement.JdbcMysqlConnection; 
public class RetriveClobDate { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Connection connection = null; 
  PreparedStatement prepareStatement = null; 
  ResultSet resultSet =null; 
  JdbcMysqlConnection jdbcConnection = new JdbcMysqlConnection(); 
  try { 
   connection = jdbcConnection.getJdbcMysqlConnection(); 
   String selectQuery = "Select Sid,SName,Cityinfo from 
testschema.studentidientity where Cityinfo is not null"; 
   if(connection!=null) 
   { 
    prepareStatement  = connection.prepareStatement(selectQuery); 
    if(prepareStatement!=null)   
    { 
     resultSet = prepareStatement.executeQuery();           
     if(resultSet!=null) 
     { 
      int counter =1; 
      while(resultSet.next()) 
      { 
       Integer sid = resultSet.getInt(1); 
       String name = resultSet.getString(2); 
       Reader reader = resultSet.getCharacterStream(3); 
       File file = new 
File("D:\\SQL\\SqlBlob\\Db_Dowload_File_"+counter+".txt"); 
       PrintWriter printWriter = new PrintWriter(file); 
     //byte buffer[] = new byte[2048]; ||    while(i!=-1){ 
     //while(ins.read(buffer)>0)       || fos.write(i); 
     //{          || i=ins.read(); 
     //  fos.write(buffer);           ||   }fos.flush(); 
     //}          || 
          IOUtils.copy(reader, printWriter); 
          printWriter.flush(); 
       counter++; 
       System.out.println(sid+" \t "+name); 
       System.out.println("File is saved to the location:: " 
+file.getAbsolutePath()); 
      } 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  }catch (SQLException|FileNotFoundException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  catch (Exception e) { 
   // hanlding logic of exception related to common problem 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  }finally { 
   jdbcConnection.closeConnection(null, prepareStatement, connection); 
  } 
 } 
}

Connection Pooling: 
* If we required to communicate with database multiple times then it is not recommended to create separate 
Connection object every time, b'z creating and destroying Connection 
object every time creates performance problems. 
* To overcome this problem, we should go for Connection Pool. 
* Connection Pool is a pool of already created Connection objects which are ready to use. 
* If we want to communicate with database then we request Connection pool to provide Connection. Once we got the 
Connection, by using that we can communicates with database. 
*After completing our work, we can return Connection to the pool instead of destroying.Hence the main advantage of 
Connection Pool is we can reuse same Connection object multiple times, so that overall performance of application 
will be improved. 
Process to implement Connection Pooling: 
1. Creation of DataSource object DataSource is responsible to manage connections in Connection Pool. DataSource is 
an interface present in javax.sql package. Driver Software vendor is responsible to provide implementation.Oracle 
people provided implementation class name is :OracleConnectionPoolDataSource. 
This class present inside oracle.jdbc.pool package and it is the part of ojdbc6.jar.  
OracleConnectionPoolDataSource ds= new OracleConnectionPoolDataSource(); 
MySqlConnectionPoolDataSource ds= new MySqlConnectionPoolDataSource(); 
2. Set required JDBC Properties to the DataSource object: 
ds.setURL("jdbc:oracle:thin:@localhost:1521:XE"); 
ds.setUser("scott"); 
ds.setPassword("tiger"); 
3. Get Connection from DataSource object: 
Connection con = ds.getConnection(); 
Once we got Connection object then remaining process is as usual. 
Note: 
This way of implementing Connection Pool is useful for Standalone applications. In 
the case of web and enterprise 
applications, we have to use server level connection pooling. Every web and 
application server can provide support for 
Connection Pooling. 
Connection Pool in JDBC 
A Connection Pool is a collection of pre-created database connections that can be reused by 
applications to improve performance and reduce overhead caused by frequently opening and closing 
database connections. 
In JDBC, using a connection pool involves leveraging a library or framework (like HikariCP, Apache 
DBCP, or C3P0) that manages the pool of database connections. 
Why Use Connection Pooling? 
Improves Performance: 
Avoids the overhead of repeatedly establishing and tearing down database connections. 
Efficient Resource Utilization: 
Limits the number of simultaneous connections to the database, avoiding resource exhaustion. 
Thread Safety: 
Allows multiple threads to reuse a limited number of connections safely. 
Steps to Use Connection Pooling in JDBC 
Add a Connection Pool Library: 
Use libraries like HikariCP, Apache DBCP, or C3P0. 
For this example, we'll use HikariCP. 
Q. What is the difference Between getting Connection object by using DriverManager 
and DataSource object? 
* In the case of DriverManager.getConnection(), always a new Connection object will be created 
and returned. 
* But in the case of DataSourceObject.getConnection(), a new Connection object won't be created 
and existing Connection object will be returned from Connection Pool. 
StoredProcedure: 
In our program,if we have any code which is repeatedly required, then we write that code inside 
function and we call that function mulitple times as per our needs.so we say functions are reusablity 
component. similary in database requirement, if we want set of sqlqueries which are repetadly 
used,then we write those set of statements in single group and we call that group based on our 
requirement. This group of sql statements only we call as "StoredProcedure". This storedprocedure 
is stored inside dbengine permanently and we need to just make a call to it. 
Store Procedure Example: 
CREATE DEFINER=`root`@`localhost` PROCEDURE `GetStudentDetailsByAge`(IN inputAge INT) 
BEGIN 
    SELECT  ts.SID, ts.StudentName, ts.StudentCourse, ts.StudentAge, ts.StudentHomeCity, ts.DateOfJoining, 
tsid.Simage, tsid.Cityinfo 
    FROM  
        testschema.students ts 
    INNER JOIN  
        testschema.studentidientity tsid  
    ON  
        ts.SID = tsid.SID 
    WHERE  
        ts.StudentAge = inputAge; 
END 
package ConnectionPool; 
import java.io.File; 
public class ConnectPoolExample { 
 public static void main(String[] args) throws SQLException, IOException { 
  MysqlConnectionPoolDataSource datasrc = new MysqlConnectionPoolDataSource(); 
  datasrc.setUrl("jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testschema"); 
  datasrc.setUser("***"); 
  datasrc.setPassword("****"); 
  PreparedStatement preparestatement = null; 
  ResultSet resultset = null; 
  Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
  System.out.print("Fetch by age Enter the Age :: "); 
  Integer age = sc.nextInt(); 
  // logical connection bought from connection pool 
  Connection connection = datasrc.getConnection(); 
  String query = "{CALL GetStudentDetailsByAge(?)}"; 
  if (connection != null) { 
   preparestatement = connection.prepareCall(query); 
   System.out.println("Query  :: " + query); 
   if (preparestatement != null) { 
    preparestatement.setInt(1, age); 
    resultset = preparestatement.executeQuery(); 
    if (resultset != null) { 
     while (resultset.next()) { 
      Integer Sid = resultset.getInt(1); 
      String sname = resultset.getString(2); 
      String cource = resultset.getString(3); 
      Integer sage = resultset.getInt(4); 
      String city = resultset.getString(5); 
      Date doj = resultset.getDate(6); 
      InputStream ins = resultset.getBinaryStream(7); 
      if (ins != null) { 
        File file = new File("D:\\SQL\\SqlBlob\\Db_Dowload_image_Fq.png"); 
       FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream(file); 
       IOUtils.copy(ins, fos); 
       ins.close(); 
      System.out.println("Image Dowloaded Path :: " + file.getAbsolutePath()); 
      } else { 
       System.out.println("Image not avalinle in Blob..."); 
      } 
      Reader reader = resultset.getCharacterStream(8); 
      if (reader != null) { 
     File txtfile = new File("D:\\SQL\\SqlBlob\\Db_Dowload Textfile.txt"); 
       PrintWriter writer = new PrintWriter(txtfile); 
       IOUtils.copy(reader, writer); 
       writer.flush(); 
       writer.close(); 
     System.out.println("File Dowloaded Path :: " + txtfile.getAbsolutePath()); 
      } else { 
       System.out.println("File not avalinle in Clob..."); 
      } 
      System.out.println("Sid : " + Sid); 
      System.out.println("StudentName : " + sname); 
      System.out.println("Cource : " + cource); 
      System.out.println("Student Age : " + sage); 
      System.out.println("Home City  : " + city); 
      System.out.println("Doj : " + doj); 
      System.out.println(); 
     }} 
    resultset.close(); 
    connection.close(); 
   }} 
  sc.close(); 
 } 
}

CREATE DEFINER=`root`@`localhost` PROCEDURE `GetStudentDetailsandCount`( 
    IN Sage INT,OUT Count INT,OUT stdName VARCHAR(20),OUT stdCrc VARCHAR(20) 
) 
BEGIN 
    -- First, select the count of records for the given Sage (Student Age) 
    SELECT COUNT(*) INTO Count FROM testschema.students ts INNER JOIN testschema.studentidientity tsid ON  
   ts.SID = tsid.SID WHERE ts.StudentAge = Sage; 
    -- Now select the first student's name and course for the given Sage 
    SELECT ts.StudentName,ts.StudentCourse INTO stdName, stdCrc FROM  
 testschema.students ts INNER JOIN testschema.studentidientity tsid ON ts.SID = tsid.SID 
    WHERE ts.StudentAge = Sage 
    LIMIT 1; -- Return only one student's name and course 
END

Code Example 
package ConnectionPool; 
import java.sql.CallableStatement; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.sql.Types; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
import com.mysql.cj.jdbc.MysqlConnectionPoolDataSource; 
public class ConnectionPool2 { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        MysqlConnectionPoolDataSource datasrc = new MysqlConnectionPoolDataSource(); 
        datasrc.setUrl("jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testschema"); 
        datasrc.setUser("****"); 
        datasrc.setPassword("****"); 
        try (Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in)) { 
            System.out.print("Fetch by Age. Enter the age: "); 
            int sage = sc.nextInt(); 
            try (Connection connection = datasrc.getConnection(); 
                 CallableStatement callablestatement = connection.prepareCall("{CALL 
GetStudentDetailsandCount(?, ?, ?, ?)}")) { 
                // Set input parameter (Sage) 
                callablestatement.setInt(1, sage); 
                // Register output parameters 
                callablestatement.registerOutParameter(2, Types.INTEGER);  // For Count 
                callablestatement.registerOutParameter(3, Types.VARCHAR);  // For stdName 
                callablestatement.registerOutParameter(4, Types.VARCHAR);  // For stdCrc 
                // Execute the stored procedure 
                callablestatement.execute(); 
                // Retrieve and print the output parameters 
                int count = callablestatement.getInt(2); 
                String studentName = callablestatement.getString(3); 
                String studentCourse = callablestatement.getString(4); 
                // Print the results 
                System.out.println("Count: " + count); 
                System.out.println("Student Name: " + studentName); 
                System.out.println("Student Course: " + studentCourse); 
            } catch (SQLException e) { 
                System.err.println("Error: " + e.getMessage()); 
                e.printStackTrace(); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

Transaction Management in JDBC: 
Transaction management in JDBC ensures that a group of SQL statements is treated as a single unit 
of work. It maintains the integrity of the database by ensuring atomicity: either all the statements 
execute successfully (commit), or none of them take effect (rollback). 
* Process of combining all related operations into a single unit and executing on the rule "either all 
or none", is called transaction management. 
* Hence transaction is a single unit of work and it will work on the rule "either all or none". 
Case-1: Funds Transfer 
1. debit funds from sender's account 
2. credit funds into receiver's account 
All operations should be performed as a single unit only. If debit from sender's account completed 
and credit into receiver's account fails then there may be a chance of data inconsistency problems. 
Case-2: Movie Ticket Reservation 
1. Verify the status 
2. Reserve the tickets 
3. Payment 
4. issue tickets. 
All operations should be performed as a single unit only. If some operations success and some 
operations fails then there may be data inconsistency problems. 
Transaction Properties: 
Every Transaction should follow the following four ACID properties. 
1. A Atomiticity ➔ Either all operations should be done or None. 
2. C Consistency(Reliabile Data) ➔ It ensures bringing database from one consistent state to 
another consistent state. 
3. I isolation (Seperatation) ➔ Ensures that transaction is isolated from other transactions 
4. D Durability ➔ It means once transaction committed, then the results are permanent even in the 
case of system restarts, errors etc. 
Types of Transactions: 
There are two types of Transactions 
1. Local Transactions 
2. Global Transactions 
1. Local Transactions: 
All operations in a transaction are executed over same database. 
Eg: Funds transfer from one accoun to another account where both accounts in the same bank. 
2. Global Transactions: All operations is a transaction are expected over different databases. 
Eg: Funds Transfer from one account to another account and accounts are related to different banks. 
Note: 
JDBC can provide support only for local transactions.If we want global transactions then we have to 
go for EJB(Enterprise Java Bean) or Spring framework. 
 Process of Transaction Management in JDBC: 
1. Disable auto commit mode of JDBC By default auto commit mode is enabled. i.e after executing every sql query, the changes 
will be committed automatically in the database. We can disable auto commit mode as follows 
con.setAutoCommit(false); 
2. If all operations completed then we can commit the transaction by using the following method. 
con.commit(); 
3. If any sql query fails then we have to rollback operations which are already completed by using rollback() method. 
con.rollback();
