Case 1: Code Example 
Summary of the Code: 
This code is a Java application that performs a bank-like transaction between two accounts in a MySQL database. The 
program connects to a MySQL database, retrieves account information, verifies the transaction conditions, and updates 
balances using transactions with savepoints to ensure data integrity. Here's a breakdown of key components: 
1. Main Process (Transaction Handling): 
User Input:The program takes user input for the following:Sender’s Name (FromAccountHolder)Receiver’s Name 
(ToAccountHolder) Amount to transfer. 
Summary of the Code: 
This code is a Java application that performs a bank-like transaction between two accounts in a MySQL database. The 
program connects to a MySQL database, retrieves account information, verifies the transaction conditions, and updates 
balances using transactions with savepoints to ensure data integrity. Here's a breakdown of key components: 
1. Main Process (Transaction Handling): 
User Input: 
The program takes user input for the following: 
Sender’s Name (FromAccountHolder) 
Receiver’s Name (ToAccountHolder) 
Amount to transfer. 
Database Connection: 
Connects to a MySQL database with transactions handled manually using setAutoCommit(false). 
Transaction Process: 
Creates a savepoint for rollback if needed.Validates sender's balance and account existence, as well as the receiver's 
account.Updates account balances: deducts from sender and adds to receiver.Commits the transaction if successful or rolls 
back if an error occurs. 
Key Methods: 
getAccountBalance(): Retrieves account balance and ID. 
updateAccountBalance(): Updates account balance. 
getUserInfo(): Prints account details. 
Error Handling: 
Rolls back on errors and prints detailed error messages. 
Output: 
Displays transaction status and updated account details. 
package com.TransactionManagementJdbc; 
import java.sql.*; 
import java.util.*; 
public class TransactionApp { 
    public static void main(String[] args) throws SQLException { 
        Connection connection = null; 
        ResultSet resultset = null; 
        PreparedStatement prepareStatement = null; 
        String FromAccountHolder;String ToAccountHolder; 
        Float Amount;Float FromAccountBalance = null; 
        Float ToAccountBalance = null;Float AmountTransferred ; 
        int FromAccountid = 0;int ToAccountid = 0; 
        Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
        try { 
            System.out.println("Transaction Started....!"); 
            System.out.println(); 
            System.out.print("Enter the Sender Name :: "); 
            FromAccountHolder = sc.nextLine(); 
            System.out.print("Enter the Receiver Name :: "); 
            ToAccountHolder = sc.nextLine(); 
            System.out.print("Enter the Amount :: "); 
            Amount = sc.nextFloat(); 
           // Establish the connection to the database 
            connection = JdbcMysqlConnection.getJdbcMysqlConnectionFromProperties(); 
            connection.setAutoCommit(false);  // Disable auto commit for transaction control 
            System.out.println("Before Sending the Money.....!");     
            if (connection != null) { 
                // Set a savepoint to roll back to if something goes wrong 
                Savepoint savepoint = connection.setSavepoint("BeforeTransfer"); 
                // Get balance and account info for the sender (FromAccountHolder) 
                if (!FromAccountHolder.isEmpty()) { 
                    getUserInfo(connection, FromAccountHolder); 
                    Map.Entry<Float, Integer> FromaccountBalance = getAccountBalance(connection, FromAccountHolder); 
                    if (FromaccountBalance != null) { 
                        FromAccountBalance = FromaccountBalance.getKey(); 
                        FromAccountid = FromaccountBalance.getValue();   
                        if (FromAccountBalance == null) { 
                            // Rollback to the savepoint if the account doesn't exist 
                            connection.rollback(savepoint); 
                            AmountTransferred = 0.0f; 
                            System.err.println("Error: Source account does not exist."); 
                            return; 
                        }                         
                        if (FromAccountBalance < Amount) { 
                            // Rollback to the savepoint if there are insufficient funds 
                            connection.rollback(savepoint); 
                            AmountTransferred = 0.0f; 
                            System.err.println("Error: Insufficient funds in source account."); 
                            return; 
                        }}} 
                // Get balance and account info for the receiver (ToAccountHolder) 
                if (!ToAccountHolder.isEmpty()) { 
                    getUserInfo(connection, ToAccountHolder); 
                    Map.Entry<Float, Integer> ToaccountBalance = getAccountBalance(connection, ToAccountHolder); 
                    if (ToaccountBalance != null) { 
                        ToAccountBalance = ToaccountBalance.getKey(); 
                        ToAccountid = ToaccountBalance.getValue(); 
                    } 
                    if (ToAccountBalance == null) { 
                        // Rollback to the savepoint if the receiver account doesn't exist 
                        connection.rollback(savepoint);AmountTransferred = 0.0f; 
                        System.err.println("Error: Destination account does not exist."); 
                        return; 
                    }} 
                // If both accounts are valid, perform the transfer (update balances) 
                updateAccountBalance(connection, FromAccountid, FromAccountBalance - Amount); // Deduct from sender 
                updateAccountBalance(connection, ToAccountid, ToAccountBalance + Amount);   // Add to receiver 
                AmountTransferred = Amount; 
                // Commit the transaction after successful transfer 
                connection.commit(); 
                System.out.println("Transaction successfully completed of Amount :- " + AmountTransferred); 
                System.out.println(); 
                System.out.println("After Sending the Money....!"); 
                getUserInfo(connection, FromAccountHolder); 
                getUserInfo(connection, ToAccountHolder); 
            }} catch (SQLException e) { 
            // In case of SQL exception, rollback to the savepoint 
            if (connection != null) { 
                connection.rollback(); 
            } 
            e.printStackTrace(System.err); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            // In case of general exceptions, rollback to the savepoint 
            if (connection != null) { 
                connection.rollback(); 
            } 
            e.printStackTrace(System.err); 
        } finally { 
            // Close resources 
            JdbcMysqlConnection.closeConnection(resultset, prepareStatement, connection); 
            if (sc != null) { 
                sc.close(); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.PreparedStatement; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.sql.Savepoint; 
import java.util.AbstractMap; 
import java.util.Map; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
import PrepareStatement.JdbcMysqlConnection; 
    // Method to fetch account balance 
    private static Map.Entry<Float, Integer> getAccountBalance(Connection connection, String 
accountHolder) throws SQLException { 
        String query = "SELECT Balance, Sid FROM testschema.accounts WHERE Account_name = ?"; 
        try (PreparedStatement preparedStatement = connection.prepareStatement(query)) { 
            preparedStatement.setString(1, accountHolder); 
            try (ResultSet resultSet = preparedStatement.executeQuery()) { 
                if (resultSet.next()) { 
                    // Return balance and account SID as a Map.Entry 
                    Float balance = resultSet.getFloat("Balance"); 
                    Integer id = resultSet.getInt("Sid"); 
                    return new AbstractMap.SimpleEntry<Float,Integer>(balance, id); // Using SimpleEntry 
to return pair 
                } else { 
                    return null; // Account does not exist 
                } 
            } 
        } 
    } 
    // Method to fetch account balance 
    private static void getUserInfo(Connection connection, String accountHolder) throws SQLException { 
        String query = "SELECT Account_name as 'Account Holder',Balance as 'Account Balance', Sid as 
'Account Sid' FROM testschema.accounts WHERE Account_name =?"; 
        try (PreparedStatement preparedStatement = connection.prepareStatement(query)) { 
            preparedStatement.setString(1, accountHolder); 
            try (ResultSet resultSet = preparedStatement.executeQuery()) { 
                if (resultSet.next()) { 
                    String name = resultSet.getString(1); 
                    float Balance = resultSet.getFloat(2); 
                    int id = resultSet.getInt(3); 
                    System.out.println("Account Id :- " + id + "\t \t" + "Account Holder Name :- " + name 
+ "\t \t" + "Account Balance :- " + Balance); 
                } else { 
                    System.out.println("User doesn't Exits....!"); 
                } 
            } 
        } 
    } 
    // Method to update the account balance 
    private static void updateAccountBalance(Connection connection, int Sid, Float newBalance) throws 
SQLException { 
        String query = "UPDATE testschema.accounts SET Balance = ? WHERE Sid = ?"; 
        try (PreparedStatement preparedStatement = connection.prepareStatement(query)) { 
            preparedStatement.setFloat(1, newBalance); 
            preparedStatement.setInt(2, Sid); 
            int rowsUpdated = preparedStatement.executeUpdate(); 
            if (rowsUpdated == 0) { 
                System.err.println("Error updating balance for " + Sid); 
            } else { 
                System.out.println("Transaction Successful...!"); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

Store Procedure: 
Case 2: Using Sp 
CREATE DEFINER=`root`@`localhost` PROCEDURE `TransferAmount`( 
    IN FromAccountName VARCHAR(45),  
    IN ToAccountName VARCHAR(45),  
    IN Amount FLOAT,  
    OUT AmountTransferred FLOAT 
) 
BEGIN 
    DECLARE FromAccountBalance FLOAT; 
    DECLARE ToAccountBalance FLOAT; 
    DECLARE FromAccountSid INT; 
    DECLARE ToAccountSid INT; 
    -- Start a transaction 
    START TRANSACTION; 
    -- Get the balance of the source account 
    SELECT Balance, Sid INTO FromAccountBalance, FromAccountSid 
    FROM testschema.accounts 
    WHERE Account_name = FromAccountName; 
    -- Debugging output: Check the input values 
    SELECT  FromAccountSid, FromAccountName, FromAccountBalance AS DebitHolderBeforeUpdate; 
    -- Check if the source account exists 
    IF FromAccountBalance IS NULL THEN 
        -- Rollback if source account does not exist 
        ROLLBACK; 
        SET AmountTransferred = 0.0; 
        SELECT 'Error: Source account does not exist.' AS TransferStatus; 
    ELSEIF FromAccountBalance < Amount THEN 
        -- Rollback if insufficient balance 
        ROLLBACK; 
        SET AmountTransferred = 0.0; 
        SELECT 'Error: Insufficient funds in source account.' AS TransferStatus; 
    ELSE 
        -- Get the destination account SID and balance 
        SELECT Sid, Balance INTO ToAccountSid, ToAccountBalance 
        FROM testschema.accounts 
        WHERE Account_name = ToAccountName; 
        -- Debugging output: Check destination account details 
        SELECT ToAccountSid, ToAccountName, ToAccountBalance AS CreditHolderBeforeUpdate; 
        IF ToAccountSid IS NULL THEN 
            -- Rollback if the destination account does not exist 
            ROLLBACK; 
            SET AmountTransferred = 0.0; 
            SELECT 'Error: Destination account does not exist.' AS TransferStatus; 
        ELSE 
            -- Create a savepoint before making updates 
            SAVEPOINT BeforeUpdate; 
            -- Deduct the amount from the source account 
            UPDATE testschema.accounts 
            SET Balance = Balance - Amount 
            WHERE Sid = FromAccountSid; 
            -- Check the rows affected by the source account update 
            SELECT ROW_COUNT() AS 'Rows Affected by Source Account Update'; 
            -- Debugging output: Check if the update affects any rows 
            SELECT FromAccountSid,FromAccountName, Balance AS DebitHolderAfterUpdate 
            FROM testschema.accounts WHERE Sid = FromAccountSid; 
            -- If no rows were affected, it means either SID is invalid or balance is insufficient 
            IF ROW_COUNT() = 0 THEN 
                SELECT 'Error: No rows updated, possibly invalid SID or insufficient balance.' AS TransferStatus; 
                ROLLBACK TO SAVEPOINT BeforeUpdate; 
                SET AmountTransferred = 0.0; 
            ELSE 
                -- Add the amount to the destination account 
                UPDATE testschema.accounts 
                SET Balance = Balance + Amount 
                WHERE Sid = ToAccountSid; 
   -- Check the rows affected by the destination account update 
                SELECT ROW_COUNT() AS 'Rows Affected by Destination Account Update'; 
                -- Debugging output: Check if the update affects any rows 
                SELECT ToAccountSid, ToAccountName,  Balance AS CreditHolderAfterUpdate 
                FROM testschema.accounts WHERE Sid = ToAccountSid; 
                -- If no rows were affected, something went wrong with the destination update 
                IF ROW_COUNT() = 0 THEN 
                    ROLLBACK TO SAVEPOINT BeforeUpdate; 
                    SELECT 'Error: Failed to update destination account.' AS TransferStatus; 
                    SET AmountTransferred = 0.0; 
                ELSE 
                    -- Commit the transaction if all updates succeed 
                    COMMIT;        
                    -- Set the output parameter to the transferred amount 
                    SET AmountTransferred = Amount; 
                    -- Final success message 
 SELECT Amount, CONCAT('Transfer Successful to ', ToAccountName) AS TransferStatus; 
                END IF; 
            END IF; 
        END IF; 
    END IF; 
END

package com.TransactionManagementJdbc; 
import java.io.IOException; 
import java.sql.CallableStatement; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.sql.Types; 
import java.util.Scanner; 
import PrepareStatement.JdbcMysqlConnection; 
public class TransactionAppBySp { 
    public static void TransferAmount(String toAccount,String fromAccount,Float amount) throws IOException { 
        Connection connection = null; 
        CallableStatement callStmt = null; 
        ResultSet resultSet = null; 
        try { 
            // Establish connection 
            connection = JdbcMysqlConnection.getJdbcMysqlConnectionFromProperties(); 
            if (connection != null) { 
                // Prepare the stored procedure call 
                callStmt = connection.prepareCall("{CALL TransferAmount(?,?,?,?)}"); 
                // Set input parameters 
                callStmt.setString(1, fromAccount); 
                callStmt.setString(2, toAccount); 
                callStmt.setFloat(3, amount); 
                // Register output parameter 
                callStmt.registerOutParameter(4, Types.FLOAT); 
                // Execute stored procedure 
                boolean hasResultSet = callStmt.execute(); 
                // Loop through all result sets 
                while (hasResultSet) { 
                    resultSet = callStmt.getResultSet(); 
                    if (resultSet != null) { 
                        // Print the result set dynamically 
                        while (resultSet.next()) { 
                            int columns = resultSet.getMetaData().getColumnCount(); 
                          //  System.out.println("Meta Data ....> : "+resultSet.getMetaData()); 
                            for (int i = 1; i <= columns; i++) { 
                                System.out.print(resultSet.getMetaData().getColumnLabel(i) + ": " + 
resultSet.getString(i) + " | "); 
                            } 
                            System.out.println(); 
                        } 
                    } 
                    hasResultSet = callStmt.getMoreResults(); 
                } 
                // Get output parameter 
                float amountTransferred = callStmt.getFloat(4); 
                System.out.println("Amount Transferred: " + amountTransferred); 
            } 
        } catch (SQLException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            JdbcMysqlConnection.closeConnection(resultSet, callStmt, connection); 
        } 
    } 
    public static void main(String[] args) throws SQLException { 
     Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in); 
     try { 
   System.out.println("Transaction Started....!"); 
   System.out.print("Enter the Name of Person Reciver :: "); 
   String toPerson = sc.nextLine(); 
   System.out.print("Enter the Name of Person Sender :: "); 
   String fromPerson = sc.nextLine(); 
   System.out.print("Enter the Amount to Send :: "); 
   Float  amount = sc.nextFloat(); 
   TransferAmount(toPerson, fromPerson, amount);  
  }catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  finally { 
   if(sc!=null) 
   { 
    sc.close(); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
}

RowSet: 
In JDBC (Java Database Connectivity), a RowSet is an interface that extends the functionality of a 
ResultSet. It provides a more flexible, scrollable, and updatable way to manage tabular data. Unlike 
ResultSet, RowSet objects can operate without being directly connected to a database, making them 
suitable for disconnected operations. 
Note: 
ResultSet(holds the data which is used for reading purpose) 
* Using resultset we have just performed read operation(best suited) 
* Is it possible to perform update,inserte and delete operation(possible but not Recommended). 
RowSet(ALL DB vendors jar support for RowSet is not available):- 
* It is alternative to ResultSet. 
* We can use RowSet to handle a group of records in more effective way than ResultSet. 
* RowSet interface present in javax.sql package 
* RowSet is child interface of ResultSet. 
* RowSet implementations will be provided by Java vendor and database vendor. 
* By default RowSet is scrollable and updatable. 
* By default RowSet is serializable and hence we can send RowSet object across the network. But 
ResultSet object is not serializable. 
* ResultSet is connected i.e to use ResultSet compulsary database Connection must be required. 
* RowSet is disconnected. ie to use RowSet database connection is not required. 
Types of RowSets:- 
There are two types of RowSets 
1. Connected RowSets 
2. Disconnected RowSets 
Connected RowSets:- 
Connected RowSets are just like ResultSets. 
To access RowSet data compulsary connection should be available to database. 
We cannot serialize Connected RowSets. 
Eg: JdbcRowSet 
Disconnected RowSets: 
Without having Connection to the database we can access RowSet data.We can serialize Disconnected 
RowSets. 
Eg:CachedRowSet,WebRowSet 
a.FilteredRowSet 
b.JoinRowSet 
How to create RowSet objects? 
We can create different types of RowSet objects as follows 
RowSetFactory rsf = RowSetProvider.newFactory(); 
JdbcRowSet jrs = rsf.createJdbcRowSet(); 
CachedRowSet crs = rsf.createCachedRowSet(); 
WebRowSet wrs = rsf.createWebRowSet(); 
JoinRowSet jnrs = rsf.createJoinRowSet(); 
FilteredRowSet frs = rsf.createFilteredRowSet(); 
package cm.RowSet; 
import java.sql.*; 
import javax.sql.rowset.*; 
public class SampleApp { 
public static void main(String[] args) 
throws SQLException { 
//factory method which is used 
to create an object of any rowset object 
RowSetFactory factory = 
RowSetProvider.newFactory(); 
JdbcRowSet jdbcRowSet = 
factory.createJdbcRowSet(); 
CachedRowSet cachedRowSet = 
factory.createCachedRowSet(); 
FilteredRowSet filteredRowSet = 
factory.createFilteredRowSet(); 
JoinRowSet joinRowSet = 
factory.createJoinRowSet(); 
WebRowSet webRowSet = 
factory.createWebRowSet(); 
} 
package cm.RowSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import javax.sql.rowset.JdbcRowSet; 
import javax.sql.rowset.RowSetFactory; 
import javax.sql.rowset.RowSetProvider; 
public class RowSetApp { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        RowSetFactory factory; 
        try { 
            factory = RowSetProvider.newFactory(); 
            try (JdbcRowSet jdbcRowSet = factory.createJdbcRowSet()) { 
                // Database connection setup 
                jdbcRowSet.setUrl("jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testschema"); 
                jdbcRowSet.setUsername("root"); 
                jdbcRowSet.setPassword("2580"); 
                jdbcRowSet.setCommand("SELECT * FROM testschema.accounts"); 
                jdbcRowSet.execute(); 
                // Forward Traversal 
                System.out.println("Student details in forward direction"); 
                System.out.println("SID\tSNAME\t\tStudBalance"); 
                System.out.println("------------------------------"); 
                while (jdbcRowSet.next()) { 
                    System.out.println(jdbcRowSet.getInt(1) + "\t" + jdbcRowSet.getString(2) + "\t" + 
jdbcRowSet.getFloat(3)); 
                } 
                System.out.println(); 
                // Backward Traversal 
                System.out.println("Student details in backward direction"); 
                System.out.println("SID\tSNAME\t\tStudBalance"); 
                System.out.println("------------------------------"); 
                while (jdbcRowSet.previous()) { 
                    System.out.println(jdbcRowSet.getInt(1) + "\t" + jdbcRowSet.getString(2) + "\t" + 
jdbcRowSet.getFloat(3)); 
                } 
                // Insert Operation 
                System.out.println("\nInserting a new record..."); 
                jdbcRowSet.moveToInsertRow(); 
                jdbcRowSet.updateInt(1, 29); 
                jdbcRowSet.updateString(2, "Rohit"); 
                jdbcRowSet.updateFloat(3, 382333.33f); 
                jdbcRowSet.insertRow(); 
                System.out.println("Record inserted successfully."); 
                // Update Operation 
                System.out.println("\nUpdating the first record..."); 
                if (jdbcRowSet.absolute(1)) { // Moves to the first row 
                    jdbcRowSet.updateString(2, "Sai Teja"); 
                    jdbcRowSet.updateFloat(3, 400000.00f); 
                    jdbcRowSet.updateRow(); 
                    System.out.println("Row updated successfully!"); 
                } else { 
                    System.out.println("No row found to update."); 
                } 
                // Delete Operation 
                System.out.println("\nDeleting the 19th record..."); 
                if (jdbcRowSet.absolute(19)) { // Check if the row exists 
                 System.out.println(jdbcRowSet.getString(2)); 
                 jdbcRowSet.deleteRow(); 
                    System.out.println("Row deleted successfully."); 
                } else { 
                    System.out.println("No 19th row exists to delete."); 
                } 
            } 
        } catch (SQLException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } 
    } 
}

JDBC Stand Alone End to Project 
This image explains CRUD Operations using Design Patterns and a Layered Approach for a Standalone Java 
Application. It showcases a three-layered architecture: 
Architecture Overview 
Controller Layer (Servlet-based) – Handles client requests and responses. 
Service Layer (Java API) – Implements business logic. 
Persistence (DAO) Layer (JDBC-based) – Interacts with the database. 
Workflow 
The client sends a request, which is processed through the Controller Layer. 
The request is passed to the Service Layer, which applies business logic. 
Finally, the DAO (Persistence) Layer interacts with the database to perform CRUD operations. 
Responses are sent back through the same layers. 
Key Concepts 
Factory Design Pattern is used to create objects for classes that implement interfaces, achieving Abstraction. 
Loose Coupling is maintained using Interfaces and Implementations. 
Dependency Injection (DI) is used to connect the layers dynamically. 
Project Requirements (Project-2) 
HikariCP for database connection pooling. 
Statement Object for executing SQL queries. 
DTO (Data Transfer Object) for transferring data between layers. 
POJI-POJO Implementation (Plain Old Java Interface / Object). 
This approach ensures scalability, maintainability, and modularity in Java-based applications. 
First Student Dto Class Should Be Created under the Project.Dto Packeage (DTO – Data 
Transfer Object): 
package in.Project.Dto; 
import java.io.Serializable;       
import java.sql.Date; 
public class StudentDtos implements Serializable 
package in.Project.Dto; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import java.sql.Date; 
public class StudentDtos implements Serializable{ 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 private Integer sid; 
 private String name; 
 private String course; 
 private Integer age; 
 private String city; 
 private Date  doj; 
 /** 
  * @param name * @param course* @param age * @param city * @param doj 
  */ 
 public StudentDtos() 
 { 
  System.out.println("StudentsDtos Object is created....."); 
 } 
 public StudentDtos(String name, String course, Integer age, String city, Date doj) { 
  this.name = name; 
  this.course = course; 
  this.age = age; 
  this.city = city; 
  this.doj = doj; 
 } 
 public String getName() { 
  return name; 
 } 
 public void setName(String name) { 
  this.name = name; 
 } 
 public String getCourse() { 
  return course; 
 } 
 public void setCourse(String course) { 
  this.course = course; 
 } 
 public Integer getAge() { 
  return age; 
 } 
 public void setAge(Integer age) { 
  this.age = age; 
 } 
 public String getCity() { 
  return city; 
 } 
 public void setCity(String city) { 
  this.city = city; 
 } 
 public Date getDoj() { 
  return doj; 
 } 
 public void setDoj(Date doj) { 
  this.doj = doj; 
 } 
 public Integer getSid() { 
  return sid; 
 } 
 public void setSid(Integer sid) { 
  this.sid = sid; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "StudentDtos [sid=" + sid + ", name=" + name + ", course=" + course + ", age=" + age + ", city=" 
+ city 
    + ", doj=" + doj + "]"; 
 } 
} 
JDBC Utils Class is Created to Connect the Data base and in Properties file data base cridentials 
were passed. In in.project Utils Package 
package in.ProjectUtils; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.IOException; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.DriverManager; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import java.util.Properties; 
import com.zaxxer.hikari.HikariConfig; 
import com.zaxxer.hikari.HikariDataSource; 
public class JdbcUtil { 
 private JdbcUtil() 
 { 
 } 
 static { 
  try { 
   Class.forName("com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver"); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
 } 
 public static Connection getJdbcConnection() throws SQLException 
 { 
  HikariConfig config = new 
HikariConfig("src\\main\\java\\in\\ProjectUtils\\db.properties"); 
  Connection connection =null; 
  try { 
   HikariDataSource dataSource = new HikariDataSource(config); 
      connection = dataSource.getConnection(); 
   return connection; 
  }catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  return connection; 
 } 
 public static Connection getJdbcPhysicalConnection() throws SQLException, IOException 
 { 
  FileInputStream fis = new  
FileInputStream("src\\main\\java\\in\\ProjectUtils\\db.properties"); 
  Properties properties = new Properties(); 
  properties.load(fis); 
  String url = properties.getProperty("url"); 
  String username = properties.getProperty("username"); 
  String password = properties.getProperty("password"); 
  Connection connection = DriverManager.getConnection(url, username, password); 
  return connection; 
 } 
}

interface IpStudentDao 
package in.Project.Dao; 
import in.Project.Dto.StudentDtos; 
public interface IpStudentDao { 
 String save(StudentDtos student);//Create a record 
 StudentDtos findById(Integer sid);// read/search by id; 
 StudentDtos findByIdName(String name);// read/search by name; 
 String updateById(StudentDtos student);// updateing a record; 
 String deleteById(Integer id);// Deleting a record 
} 
class StudentDaoImplementation implements IpStudentDao 
package in.Project.Dao; 
import java.sql.Connection; 
import java.sql.PreparedStatement; 
import java.sql.ResultSet; 
import java.sql.SQLException; 
import in.Project.Dto.StudentDtos; 
import in.ProjectUtils.JdbcUtil; 
public class StudentDaoImplementation implements IpStudentDao { 
 Connection connection = null; 
 @Override 
 public String save(StudentDtos student) { 
  String sqlInsertQuery = "INSERT INTO testschema.students (`StudentName`, 
`StudentCourse`, `StudentAge`, `StudentHomeCity`,`DateOfJoining`)VALUES (?, ?, ?, 
?,?);"; 
  PreparedStatement prepareStatement = null; 
  String status = null; 
  try { 
   connection = JdbcUtil.getJdbcConnection(); 
   System.out.println("Impl Class : " + connection.getClass().getName()); 
   if (connection != null) { 
    prepareStatement = connection.prepareStatement(sqlInsertQuery); 
    if (prepareStatement != null) { 
     prepareStatement.setString(1, student.getName()); 
     prepareStatement.setString(2, student.getCourse()); 
     prepareStatement.setInt(3, student.getAge()); 
     prepareStatement.setString(4, student.getCity()); 
     prepareStatement.setDate(5, student.getDoj()); 
    } 
    if (prepareStatement != null) { 
     int RowsEffected = prepareStatement.executeUpdate(); 
     if (RowsEffected == 1) { 
      status = "success"; 
     } else { 
      status = "failure"; 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   status = "failure"; 
  } 
  return status; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public StudentDtos findById(Integer sid) { 
  String selectbyIdQuery = "SELECT 
SID,StudentName,StudentCourse,StudentAge,StudentHomeCity,DateOfJoining FROM testschema.students where 
SID =?"; 
  PreparedStatement prepareStatement = null; 
  StudentDtos students = null; 
  try { 
   Connection connection = JdbcUtil.getJdbcConnection(); 
   if (connection != null) { 
    prepareStatement = connection.prepareStatement(selectbyIdQuery); 
    if (prepareStatement != null) { 
     prepareStatement.setInt(1, sid); 
     ResultSet resultset = prepareStatement.executeQuery(); 
     while (resultset.next()) { 
      students = new StudentDtos(); 
      students.setSid(resultset.getInt(1)); 
      students.setName(resultset.getString(2)); 
      students.setCourse(resultset.getString(3)); 
      students.setAge(resultset.getInt(4)); 
      students.setCity(resultset.getString(5)); 
      students.setDoj(resultset.getDate(6)); 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (SQLException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  return students; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public StudentDtos findByIdName(String name) { 
  String selectbyIdQuery = "SELECT 
SID,StudentName,StudentCourse,StudentAge,StudentHomeCity,DateOfJoining FROM testschema.students where 
StudentName=?"; 
  PreparedStatement prepareStatement = null; 
  StudentDtos students = null; 
  try { 
   Connection connection = JdbcUtil.getJdbcConnection(); 
   if (connection != null) { 
    prepareStatement = connection.prepareStatement(selectbyIdQuery); 
    if (prepareStatement != null) { 
     prepareStatement.setString(1, name); 
     ResultSet resultset = prepareStatement.executeQuery(); 
     while (resultset.next()) { 
      students = new StudentDtos(); 
      students.setSid(resultset.getInt(1)); 
      students.setName(resultset.getString(2)); 
      students.setCourse(resultset.getString(3)); 
      students.setAge(resultset.getInt(4)); 
      students.setCity(resultset.getString(5)); 
      students.setDoj(resultset.getDate(6)); 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (SQLException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  return students; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String updateById(StudentDtos student) { 
  String SqlupdateQuery = "UPDATE testschema.students SET StudentName =?, StudentCourse =?, 
StudentAge =?, StudentHomeCity =?, DateOfJoining =? WHERE SID = ?"; 
  PreparedStatement prepareStatement = null; 
  String status = null; 
  try { 
   Connection connection = JdbcUtil.getJdbcConnection(); 
   if (connection != null) { 
    prepareStatement = connection.prepareStatement(SqlupdateQuery); 
    if (prepareStatement != null) { 
     prepareStatement.setString(1, student.getName()); 
     prepareStatement.setString(2, student.getCourse()); 
     prepareStatement.setInt(3, student.getAge()); 
     prepareStatement.setString(4, student.getCity()); 
     prepareStatement.setDate(5, student.getDoj()); // Ensure `getDoj()` 
returns `java.sql.Date` 
     prepareStatement.setInt(6, student.getSid()); 
     System.out.println("STD SID :: " + student.getSid()); 
    } 
    if (prepareStatement != null) { 
     int RowCount = prepareStatement.executeUpdate(); // Execute update 
without passing SQL query 
     if (RowCount == 1) { 
      status = "success"; 
     } else { 
      status = "failure"; 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   status = "failure"; 
  } 
  return status; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String deleteById(Integer id) { 
  String DelectQuery = "Delete from testschema.students where SID =?"; 
  PreparedStatement prepareStatement = null; 
  String status = null; 
  try { 
   Connection connection = JdbcUtil.getJdbcConnection(); 
   if (connection != null) { 
    prepareStatement = connection.prepareStatement(DelectQuery); 
    if (prepareStatement != null) { 
     prepareStatement.setInt(1, id); 
     int rowseffected = prepareStatement.executeUpdate(); 
     if (rowseffected == 1) { 
      status = "success"; 
     } else { 
      status = "Record not avalible"; 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (SQLException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   status = "failure"; 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   status = "failure"; 
  } 
  return status; 
 } 
}

class StudentDaoFactory 
package in.ProjectFactory; 
import in.Project.Dao.IpStudentDao; 
import in.Project.Dao.StudentDaoImplementation;

 { 
 }

class StudentServiceImplementation implements IpStudentService 
package in.ProjectService;

 public String save(StudentDtos student) { 
  studentDao = StudentDaoFactory.getStudentDao(); 
  System.out.println("Imp class Name : "+ studentDao.getClass().getName()); 
  return studentDao.save(student); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public StudentDtos findById(Integer sid) { 
  studentDao = StudentDaoFactory.getStudentDao(); 
  System.out.println("Imp class Name : "+ studentDao.getClass().getName()); 
  return studentDao.findById(sid); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public StudentDtos findByIdName(String name) { 
  studentDao = StudentDaoFactory.getStudentDao(); 
  System.out.println("Imp class Name : "+ studentDao.getClass().getName()); 
  return studentDao.findByIdName(name); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String updateById(StudentDtos student) { 
  studentDao = StudentDaoFactory.getStudentDao(); 
  System.out.println("Imp class Name : "+ studentDao.getClass().getName()); 
  return studentDao.updateById(student); 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String deleteById(Integer id) { 
  studentDao = StudentDaoFactory.getStudentDao(); 
  System.out.println("Imp class Name : "+ studentDao.getClass().getName()); 
  return studentDao.deleteById(id); 
 } 
}

AppTest Under theMain Package to Perform All Curd  DB Operation in 
a Single Class 
package in.Project.main; 
import java.io.BufferedReader; 
import java.io.InputStreamReader; 
import java.text.SimpleDateFormat; 
import java.util.Date; 
import in.Project.Controller.IpStudentController; 
import in.Project.Dto.StudentDtos; 
import in.ProjectFactory.StudentControllerFactory; 
public class Apptest { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  IpStudentController studentcontroller = null; 
  String status = null,name = null, course = null, age = null, city = null,Doj =null; 
  Integer id = null; 
  StudentDtos studentRecord = null; 
  try { 
    while(true) 
    { 
     BufferedReader br = new BufferedReader(new InputStreamReader(System.in)); 
     System.out.println("1.Create....!"); 
     System.out.println("2.Read/Select By Id....!"); 
     System.out.println("3.Read/Select By Name....!"); 
     System.out.println("4.Update....!"); 
     System.out.println("5.Delete....!"); 
     System.out.println("6.Exit....!"); 
     System.out.println("Your Option....?"); 
     System.out.println("1 or 2 or 3 or 4 or 5 or 6"); 
     studentcontroller = StudentControllerFactory.getStudentController(); 
     Integer options = Integer.parseInt(br.readLine()); 
     switch (options) { 
     case 1: 
      System.out.print("Enter the Student Name : "); 
         name = br.readLine(); 
      System.out.print("Enter the Student course : "); 
      course = br.readLine(); 
      System.out.print("Enter the Student Age : "); 
         age = br.readLine(); 
      System.out.print("Enter the Student City : "); 
         city = br.readLine(); 
      System.out.print("Enter the Student Doj : "); 
         Doj = br.readLine(); 
      StudentDtos student = new StudentDtos(); 
      student.setName(name); 
      student.setCourse(course); 
      student.setAge(Integer.parseInt(age)); 
      student.setCity(city); 
       // Define the date format 
      java.sql.Date dojsqDate = null; 
            try { 
               SimpleDateFormat sdf = new SimpleDateFormat("yyyy-MM-dd"); 
            Date dojdate = sdf.parse(Doj); 
            dojsqDate = new java.sql.Date(dojdate.getTime()); 
      } catch (Exception e) { 
       e.printStackTrace(); 
      } 
            student.setDoj(dojsqDate); 
            status = studentcontroller.save(student); 
            if(status.equalsIgnoreCase("success")) 
            { 
             System.out.println("Record Inserted Sucessfully......."); 
            }else if(status.equalsIgnoreCase("failure")) 
            { 
             System.out.println("Record Insertation Failed....."); 
            } 
            else 
            { 
             System.out.println("Some other problem occured please try Again After 
Some time.....!"); 
            } 
      break; 
 case 2: 
  System.out.println("Find/Select By Id...Please Enter the UserId:"); 
      id = Integer.parseInt(br.readLine()); 
      studentRecord = studentcontroller.findById(id); 
      if(studentRecord!=null) 
      { 
       System.out.println(studentRecord.toString()); 
      } 
      else 
      { 
 System.out.println("Student record is not avalible on this particular id "); 
      } 
      break; 
     case 3: 
 System.out.print("Find/Select By Name...Please Enter the UserName:"); 
      name = br.readLine(); 
      studentRecord = studentcontroller.findByIdName(name); 
      if(studentRecord!=null) 
      { 
       System.out.println(studentRecord.toString()); 
      } 
      else 
      { 
  System.out.println("Student record is not avalible on this particular name "); 
      } 
      break; 
     case 4: 
       System.out.print("Enter the Record Id to Update :: "); 
          id = Integer.parseInt(br.readLine()); 
          studentRecord = studentcontroller.findById(id); 
          if (studentRecord != null) { 
              StudentDtos newStudent = new StudentDtos(); 
              newStudent.setSid(id); 
              // Update Name 
System.out.print("Student name <--> [Old Name is :: " + studentRecord.getName() + "] :"); 
              String newName = br.readLine(); 
              if (newName == null || newName.trim().isEmpty()) { 
                  newStudent.setName(studentRecord.getName()); 
              } else { 
                  newStudent.setName(newName); 
              } 
              // Update Course 
   System.out.print("Student Course <--> [Old Course is :: " + studentRecord.getCourse() + "] :"); 
              String newCourse = br.readLine(); 
              if (newCourse == null || newCourse.trim().isEmpty()) { 
                  newStudent.setCourse(studentRecord.getCourse()); 
              } else { 
                  newStudent.setCourse(newCourse); 
              } 
              // Update Age 
  System.out.print("Student Age <--> [Old Age is :: " + studentRecord.getAge() + "] :"); 
              String newAgeStr = br.readLine(); 
              if (newAgeStr == null || newAgeStr.trim().isEmpty()) { 
                  newStudent.setAge(studentRecord.getAge()); 
              } else { 
                  Integer newAge = Integer.parseInt(newAgeStr); 
                  newStudent.setAge(newAge); 
              } 
              // Update City 
System.out.print("Student City <--> [Old City Name is :: " + studentRecord.getCity() + "] :"); 
              String newCity = br.readLine(); 
              if (newCity == null || newCity.trim().isEmpty()) { 
                  newStudent.setCity(studentRecord.getCity()); 
              } else { 
                  newStudent.setCity(newCity);  // Fix: Set City instead of 
Course 
              } 
              // Update Date of Joining (DOJ) 
 System.out.print("Student DOJ <--> [Old DOJ is :: " + studentRecord.getDoj() + "] :"); 
              String newDojstr = br.readLine(); 
              if (newDojstr == null || newDojstr.trim().isEmpty()) { 
                  newStudent.setDoj(studentRecord.getDoj());  // Keep  
              }  
else { 
                  try { 
                      // Parse the new DOJ string into a 
java.sql.Date (assumes format "yyyy-mm-dd") 
                      java.sql.Date newDoj = 
java.sql.Date.valueOf(newDojstr); 
                      newStudent.setDoj(newDoj); 
                  } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) { 
                      System.out.println("Invalid date format. Please 
enter a date in yyyy-mm-dd format."); 
                      return; // Exit or continue to handle the error 
appropriately 
                  } 
              } 
       status = studentcontroller.updateById(newStudent); 
       if(status.equalsIgnoreCase("success")) 
       { 
        System.out.println("Record Data Updated 
Sucessfully......"); 
       } 
       else if(status.equalsIgnoreCase("failure")) 
       { 
        System.out.println("Record Data Updatation 
Failed......"); 
       } 
       else 
       { 
        System.out.println("Record not available for the 
given id to Update..."); 
       } 
      }  
      break; 
     case 5: 
      System.out.println("Delect By Id...Please Enter the UserId:"); 
      id = Integer.parseInt(br.readLine()); 
      status = studentcontroller.deleteById(id); 
       if(status.equalsIgnoreCase("success")) 
       { 
       System.out.println("Record Delected 
Sucessfully......."); 
       } else if (status.equalsIgnoreCase("failure")) { 
       System.out.println("Record Delection Failed....."); 
       } else { 
        System.out.println("Record not available for the 
given id to delete..."); 
       }  
      break; 
     case 6: 
      System.out.println("Thank for using this Application......."); 
      System.exit(0); 
     default: 
      System.out.println("Please the Select the Option from 1 to5 for 
to perform Actions "); 
      break; 
     } 
    } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
  } 
 } 
}

Introduction to Hibernate 
What is Hibernate? 
Hibernate is a Java-based ORM (Object-Relational Mapping) framework that simplifies database 
interactions by mapping Java objects to database tables. It eliminates the need for writing complex 
SQL queries and provides a more flexible and efficient way to work with databases in Java 
applications. 
Key Features of Hibernate 
ORM (Object-Relational Mapping): 
Maps Java objects (POJOs) to database tables automatically. 
Eliminates the need for boilerplate JDBC code. 
HQL (Hibernate Query Language): 
A powerful query language similar to SQL but operates on Java objects instead of tables. 
Automatic Table Creation: 
Hibernate can automatically generate tables based on entity classes. 
Lazy and Eager Loading: 
Supports both lazy loading (fetches data only when needed) and eager loading (fetches data immediately). 
Transaction Management: 
Supports ACID transactions with commit and rollback mechanisms. 
Caching Mechanism: 
Uses first-level and second-level caching to improve performance. 
Database Independence: 
Works with multiple databases (MySQL, PostgreSQL, Oracle, etc.) without changing the code. 
Why Use Hibernate? 
✅ Reduces Boilerplate Code – No need for repetitive JDBC code. 
✅ Improves Performance – Optimized queries and caching mechanisms. 
✅ Portable and Scalable – Works with different databases easily. 
✅ Supports Annotations & XML Configurations – Flexible configuration options. 
Architecture of Hibernate 
 Configuration – Defines database connection settings (hibernate.cfg.xml). 
 SessionFactory – Creates Session objects (thread-safe). 
 Session – Handles database operations. 
 Transaction – Manages commit/rollback of queries. 
 Query – Executes HQL or Criteria queries. 
 JDBC Connection – Communicates with the database. 
<hibernate-configuration> 
<session-factory> 
<property name="hibernate.connection.driver_class">com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver</property> 
<property name="hibernate.connection.url">jdbc:mysql://localhost:3306/testdb</property> 
<property name="hibernate.connection.username">root</property> 
<property name="hibernate.connection.password">password</property> 
<property name="hibernate.dialect">org.hibernate.dialect.MySQL8Dialect</property> 
<property name="hibernate.hbm2ddl.auto">update</property> 
<property name="hibernate.show_sql">true</property> 
</session-factory> 
</hibernate-configuration> 
import javax.persistence.*; 
@Entity 
@Table(name = "students") 
public class Student { 
@Id 
@GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY) 
private int id; 
private String name; 
private String email; 
// Getters and Setters 
public int getId() { return id; } 
public void setId(int id) { this.id = id; } 
Basic Code Example 
import org.hibernate.SessionFactory; 
import org.hibernate.cfg.Configuration; 
public class HibernateUtil { 
private static final SessionFactory sessionFactory = 
new Configuration() 
.configure("hibernate.cfg.xml") 
.buildSessionFactory(); 
} 
public static SessionFactory getSessionFactory() { 
return sessionFactory; 
} 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
public class Main { 
public static void main(String[] args) { 
Session session = HibernateUtil.getSessionFactory().openSession(); 
Transaction tx = session.beginTransaction(); 
public String getName() { return name; } 
public void setName(String name) { this.name = name; } 
// Create Student Object 
Student student = new Student(); 
student.setName("John Doe"); 
student.setEmail("john@example.com"); 
// Save to Database 
session.save(student); 
tx.commit(); 
session.close(); 
System.out.println("Student Saved Successfully!"); 
public String getEmail() { return email; } 
public void setEmail(String email) { this.email = email; } 
} 
Hibernate Design and Internal Mapping for ORM 
Hibernate's design and its internal mapping mechanisms are at the core of how it transforms Java 
objects into relational database records and vice versa. Understanding these key points can help you 
appreciate how Hibernate efficiently manages object-relational mapping (ORM) tasks. Below are the 
essential design aspects and internal mapping details of Hibernate: 
1.Core Architecture 
 a.Configuration and Metadata Processing: 
  1.Configuration Phase: 
  Hibernate starts by reading configuration settings from XML files (like hibernate.cfg.xml) or through               
  annotations. This configuration includes database connection properties, dialect information, and 
  mapping definitions. 
  2.Metadata Processing: 
  Hibernate processes mapping metadata from XML files or annotations. It converts this metadata into 
  an internal representation (e.g., instances of PersistentClass and Collection mappings) that defines how 
  each Java class and its properties relate to database tables and columns. 
b. SessionFactory and Session 
 SessionFactory: 
 A heavyweight, thread-safe object created during application initialization. It holds the 
 compiled mapping metadata and is responsible for opening lightweight Session objects. 
 Session: 
 Represents a single-threaded unit of work. It acts as a cache (first-level cache) and manages 
 the persistence life cycle of objects. It is responsible for CRUD operations, query execution, 
 and transaction management. 
2. Internal Mapping Mechanisms 
 a. Entity Mapping 
  PersistentClass Representation: 
  Each entity class is mapped to a database table. Internally, Hibernate uses a   
  PersistentClass object to represent the entity’s metadata, which includes its properties, 
  identifiers, and association mappings. 
  Property and Column Mapping: 
  Each property in the entity (fields or getter/setter pairs) is mapped to one or more  
  columns in the corresponding table. Hibernate supports different strategies for property 
  mapping, such as: 
   Simple Types: Mapping basic Java types (e.g., String, int) to SQL types. 
   Custom Types: Allowing custom mapping logic through user-defined types. 
 b. Association Mapping: 
  One-to-One, One-to-Many, Many-to-One, and Many-to-Many: 
  Hibernate provides support for different association types. Internally: 
  Foreign Key Associations: Hibernate uses foreign key columns to manage   
  relationships. 
  Join Tables: For many-to-many relationships, join tables are used to manage the  
  association. 
  Lazy Loading and Proxies: 
           Hibernate utilizes proxies and bytecode instrumentation to implement lazy loading. This 
           means that associated entities are fetched only when accessed, reducing the overhead of 
           unnecessary data retrieval. 
         c. Inheritance Mapping 
 Hibernate offers several strategies to map class inheritance hierarchies: 
  Single Table Inheritance: 
  All classes in the hierarchy are mapped to a single table with a discriminator column. 
  Joined Subclass Inheritance: 
  Each class is mapped to its own table, and relationships between tables are defined by 
  foreign keys. 
  Table Per Class Inheritance: 
  Each concrete class is mapped to its own table. Although simple, it may lead to  
  redundancy and requires unions during polymorphic queries. 
3. SQL Generation and Dialect Abstraction 
 Dialect: 
 Hibernate abstracts differences between various databases through the concept of a dialect.  The 
 dialect defines how SQL is generated for a particular database system (e.g., MySQL,  Oracle). 
 This allows Hibernate to produce database-specific SQL commands based on the  mapping 
 metadata. 
 SQL Generation: 
 Using the internal metadata, Hibernate’s persisters (such as EntityPersister for entities and 
 CollectionPersister for collections) are responsible for generating SQL statements (INSERT, 
 UPDATE, DELETE, SELECT). These persisters handle the translation from object state 
 changes to the corresponding SQL operations. 
4. Caching Mechanisms 
 a. First-Level Cache (Session Cache) 
  Scope: 
  Lives within the scope of a session. Every time an object is fetched or saved in a  
  session, it is stored in this cache. This ensures that repeated requests for the same data  
  within a session do not hit the database multiple times. 
 b. Second-Level Cache 
  Scope: 
  Configurable to be shared across sessions. It caches entities, collections, and queries,  
  reducing the number of database hits for repeated queries across transactions. 
  Integration: 
  Hibernate integrates with caching providers (like Ehcache or Infinispan) to manage this 
  level of caching. 
5. Transaction Management and Concurrency 
 Unit of Work Pattern: 
 The session acts as a unit of work, encapsulating the transactional operations. Hibernate 
 ensures that all operations within a session are consistent and, if needed, can be rolled back in
 case of errors. 
 Optimistic Locking: 
 Hibernate supports versioning for entities, which allows it to detect concurrent modifications 
 and maintain data integrity in multi-user environments. 
 Dirty Checking: 
 Hibernate automatically detects changes in persistent objects and synchronizes these changes 
 with the database during the flush operation, without requiring explicit update calls from the 
 developer. 
6. Extensibility and Integration 
 Custom Types and Interceptors: 
 Developers can define custom types (via UserType or CompositeUserType) to handle  specialized 
 mapping needs. Interceptors and event listeners allow you to integrate custom  logic during the 
 ORM life cycle. 
 Pluggable Components: 
 Many parts of Hibernate’s internal processing (e.g., SQL generation, caching, transaction 
 handling)  are designed to be pluggable, allowing developers to extend or replace default 
 behavior to better fit  their application requirements. 
To Write Once application We need to use 4 files as shown in Below. 
 a.Model Class 
 b.Mapping Code --- (Xml/Annotation) 
 c.Configuration File – (Xml) 
 d.Test Class 
Model Class: 
 It Represents Model data, It can be called as Entity/Pojo. 
 Class must have Package Statement. 
 Class must not be Public type. 
 No of Tables == No of class. 
 Class can have Variable must be private. [ No of columns = =  No of variables] 
 Class Should Have Zero arguments constructor and with Setters and getters Method. 
 Class can Override to String ,Hash Code ,Equals,from Object Class. 
 Class can Have Annotations Given by JPA also Core Library Annotations. 
 Class Can In-herit(IS-A)[Extends/Implements] only by hibernate Api. 
MapCodeing : 
1.@Entity: 
 It Represntes Map model Class With Db Tables and Varibles Column Names. 
2.@ID: 
 It Iddicates Primary Key,Every Table Must Contains Primary Key Column. 
3.@Table: 
 It Indicates the Table Name which is been mapped with variable Name of a Model Class. 
4.@Column: 
 It Indicates ColumnName of the Table which is been Mapped with the Variable Name of  
 Model Class. 
Note: 
 If @Table,@Column are not provided then by default class name is Table name , variable 
 Name is Column Name ( Is Taken By hibernate). 
Example: 
@Entity 
@Table(name=”empTable”) 
Public class Employee 
{ 
 @id 
 @Column(name=”eid”) 
 Private int empid; 
 @column(name=”ename”) 
 Private String empname; 
 @column 
 Private double EmpSalary; 
} 
Example: 
@Entity 
@Table(name=”ProdTable”) 
Public class Products 
{ 
 @id 
 @Column(name=”Pid”) 
 Private int prodid; 
 @column(name=”ProdCode”) 
 Private String prodCode; 
 @column 
 Private double ProductCost; 
} 
Note: 
 <property name="dialect">org.hibernate.dialect.MySQLDialect</property> 
dialect => It is a class available inside package called org.hibernate.dialect,it will generate the SQLQuery when the 
programmer performs operation. For every database dialect is different. 
Oracle => nature of query 
MySQL  => nature of query 
PostgreSQL => nature of query 
<!-- Echo all executed SQL to stdout --> 
<property name="show_sql">true</property> 
This property is used to see the Query generated by the dialect based on the datbase environment on the console. 
<property name="format_sql">true</property> 
This property is used to fromat the Query generated by the dialect based on the datbase environment on the console. 
<property name ='hibernate.hbm2ddl.auto">[validate/create/update/create-drop]</property> 
validate =>hibernate creates no table, programmer should create or modify tables manually. this is considered as default value. 
Create  = > hibernate always creates new table,if table exists it will drop the table. 
Update  => hibernate creates new table,if table doesnot exists, otherwise it will reuse the same table. 
Create-drop =>This option is used for testing purpose not in development creates a new table and perform operation,at last it 
will drop the table. 
Test class coding and its execution flow 
 1. Create a configuration object 
 2. Load .cfg.xml file into configuration object using configure(). 
 3. Build SessionFactory object using cfg which handles 
  a. Loading driver class 
  b. Creating connection 
  c. Prepare statement objects. 
 4. use SessionFactory and get Session object to perform Persistence operation. 
 5. Begin Transaction, if the operation in Non-Select. 
 6. Now perform operation using Session object. 
 7. Commit or rollback if transaction has started. 
 8. close the session at the end. 
 Note: To specify the configuration details and mapping details we need to write xml file.if the filename is hibernate.cfg.xml 
then it promotes automatic loading,otherwise we need to read those data from "FileInputStream". 
Hibernate Architecture 
<hibernate-configuration> 
 <session-factory> 
  <property 
name="hibernate.dialect">org.hibernate.dialect.MySQL8Dialect</property> 
  <property 
name="hibernate.connection.driver_class">com.mysql.cj.jdbc.Driver</property> 
  <property name="hibernate.connection.username">root</property> 
  <property name="hibernate.connection.password">2580</property> 
  <property 
name="hibernate.connection.url">jdbc:mysql:///testschema</property> 
  <property name="hibernate.show_sql">true</property> 
  <property name="hibernate.format_sql">true</property> 
  <property name="hibernate.hbm2ddl.auto">update</property> 
  <mapping class="com.FirstHibernateProject.StudentDtos" /> 
 </session-factory> 
</hibernate-configuration> 
Hibernate Xml File 
Summary: 
This hibernate.cfg.xml file configures Hibernate to connect with a MySQL 
database (testschema). It specifies the JDBC driver, username, password, and 
SQL dialect. The hibernate.hbm2ddl.auto property is set to update to 
automatically update the database schema. SQL query logging is enabled, and 
the StudentDtos entity class is mapped to a database table. 🚀 
@Entity Class Example: 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import java.sql.Date; 
import jakarta.persistence.Column; 
import jakarta.persistence.Entity; 
import jakarta.persistence.GeneratedValue; 
import jakarta.persistence.GenerationType; 
import jakarta.persistence.Id; 
import jakarta.persistence.Table; 
@Entity 
@Table(name="students") 
public class StudentDtos implements Serializable{ 
 //StudentName`, `StudentCourse`, `StudentAge`, `StudentHomeCity`,`DateOfJoining 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 @Id 
 //@Column(name="SID") 
 @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY) 
 private Integer sid; 
 @Column(name="StudentName") 
 private String name; 
 @Column(name="StudentCourse") 
 private String course; 
 @Column(name ="StudentAge") 
 private Integer age; 
 @Column (name="StudentHomeCity") 
 private String city; 
 @Column(name ="DateOfJoining") 
 private Date  doj; 
 static  
 { 
  System.out.println("Employee Class is Loading......"); 
 } 
 public StudentDtos() 
 { 
  System.out.println("Zero Paramatrized Constructor...."); 
 } 
 public StudentDtos(String name, String course, Integer age, String city, Date doj) { 
  this.name = name; 
  this.course = course; 
  this.age = age; 
  this.city = city; 
  this.doj = doj; 
 } 
 public String getName() { 
  return name; 
 } 
 public void setName(String name) { 
  this.name = name; 
 } 
 public String getCourse() { 
  return course; 
 } 
 public void setCourse(String course) { 
  this.course = course; 
 } 
 public Integer getAge() { 
  return age; 
 } 
 public void setAge(Integer age) { 
  this.age = age; 
 } 
 public String getCity() { 
  return city; 
 } 
 public void setCity(String city) { 
  this.city = city; 
 } 
 public Date getDoj() { 
  return doj; 
 } 
 public void setDoj(Date doj) { 
  this.doj = doj; 
 } 
 public Integer getSid() { 
  return sid; 
 } 
 public void setSid(Integer sid) { 
  this.sid = sid; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "StudentDtos [sid=" + sid + ", name=" + name + ", course=" + course + ", age=" + age + ", city=" + city 
    + ", doj=" + doj + "]";} 
 } 
@Test Cass for Adding in DB: 
package com.Test; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.SessionFactory; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import org.hibernate.cfg.Configuration; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.StudentDtos; 
public class hibernateTestClass { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  //Step 1 : Creating a  new Configuration Object.. 
  Configuration config = new Configuration(); 
  //Step 2: Configure Hibernate.Cfg.Xml file to Configuration Object... 
  config.configure(); 
  //Step 3: Create a Session Factory Object by using Configuration Object... 
  //Build SessionFactory... 
  SessionFactory  sessionFactory =config.buildSessionFactory(); 
  //Step 4 : Getting the Session Object fro Session Factory.... 
  Session session =  sessionFactory.openSession(); 
  //Step 5 : Begin the Transaction with in the Session... 
  Transaction transaction = session.beginTransaction(); 
  // Step 6 : creating a Student Objects { Entity Class } to insert the Data  
  StudentDtos students = new StudentDtos(); 
  //students.setSid(17); 
  students.setName("Mark"); 
  students.setCourse("AI and Ml"); 
  students.setAge(26); 
  students.setCity("Calfornia"); 
  String newDojstr = "2014-08-27"; 
  java.sql.Date newDoj = java.sql.Date.valueOf(newDojstr); 
  students.setDoj(newDoj); 
  //Step 7 : Performing Operation/Action 
  Serializable object = (Serializable) session.save(students); 
  System.out.println(object); 
  //Step 8: Peforming Transection Operation.. 
  transaction.commit(); 
  // Step 9 : Closeing the Session... 
  session.close(); 
 } 
}

      try { 
       transaction= session.beginTransaction();// Automatically 
session.setAutoCommite(False);

       System.out.println("ID Value : "+Idvalue); 
       flag = true;

   e.printStackTrace();

Hibernate Utils Pack/Class 
package com.HibernateUtils; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.SessionFactory; 
import org.hibernate.cfg.Configuration; 
public class HibernateUtil { 
  static Configuration config = null; 
  static SessionFactory sessionfactory = null; 
  static Session session = null; 
  static 
  { 
   try { 
   config = new Configuration(); 
   config.configure(); 
   sessionfactory = config.buildSessionFactory(); 
  } 
   catch (HibernateException e) { 
    e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
   catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  public static Session getSession() 
  { 
  if(session==null) 
  { 
   session = sessionfactory.openSession(); 
  } 
  return session; 
  } 
  public static void CloseSession(Session session) 
  { 
   if(session!=null) 
   { 
    session.close(); 
   } 
  } 
  public void closeSessionFactory(SessionFactory sessionfactory) 
  { 
   if(sessionfactory!=null) 
   { 
    sessionfactory.close(); 
   } 
  } 
} 
For Single Record 
package com.dbCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.StudentDtos; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class Seslect_GetStudentData { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
  StudentDtos students = null; 
  int sid = 2; 
  try { 
   if(session!=null) 
   { 
    students = session.load(StudentDtos.class, sid); 
   } 
   System.out.println(students.toString()); 
  } catch (HibernateException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   System.out.println("Student record is ot found on this SID :: "+sid); 
  } 
  catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   System.out.println("Student record is ot found on this SID :: "+sid); 
  } 
 } 
} 
package com.dbCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.query.Query; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.StudentDtos; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
import java.util.List; 
public class SelectStudentData { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
        String name = "Hanuman";  // name you want to search for 
        try { 
            if (session != null) { 
                // Use HQL to query based on the 'name' field of StudentDtos 
                String hql = "FROM StudentDtos WHERE name = :name";  // Assuming 'name' is a field in StudentDtos class 
                Query<StudentDtos> query = session.createQuery(hql, StudentDtos.class); 
                query.setParameter("name", name); 
                // Fetch the results as a list 
                List<StudentDtos> students = query.list();  // This returns a list of students 
                if (students != null && !students.isEmpty()) { 
                    // Print each student (or handle them as needed) 
                    for (StudentDtos student : students) { 
                        System.out.println(student.toString()); 
                    } 
                } else { 
                    System.out.println("No students found with name: " + name); 
                } 
            } 
        } catch (HibernateException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
            System.out.println("Error occurred while fetching student data for name: " + name); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
            System.out.println("Error occurred while fetching student data for name: " + name); 
        } finally { 
            // Close session properly 
            if (session != null) { 
                session.close(); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

package com.dbCurdOperations; 
import java.sql.Date; 
import java.text.SimpleDateFormat; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.StudentDtos; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class InsertStudentsData { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = null; 
  Transaction transation = null; 
  boolean flag = false; 
  try { 
   session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
   if(session!=null) 
   { 
    transation = session.beginTransaction(); 
   } 
   if(transation!=null) 
   { 
    StudentDtos students = new StudentDtos(); 
    students.setName("Ronaldo"); 
    students.setCourse("Foot Ball"); 
    students.setAge(35); 
    students.setCity("Porchgies"); 
    String dojDate = "24-08-2001"; 
    SimpleDateFormat sdf = new SimpleDateFormat("dd-MM-yyyy"); 
    java.util.Date udate = sdf.parse(dojDate); 
    Date doj = new Date(udate.getTime()); 
    System.out.println("Date : "+doj); 
    students.setDoj(doj); 
    session.save(students); 
    flag =true; 
   } 
  }catch (HibernateException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  finally { 
   if(flag == true) 
   { 
    transation.commit(); 
   }else 
   { 
    transation.rollback(); 
   } 
   HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
  } 
 } 
}

Deleteing the Record: 
package com.dbCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.StudentDtos; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class DeleteData { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = null; 
  Transaction transection =null; 
  boolean flage = false; 
  try { 
   session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
   if(session!=null) 
   { 
    transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
    if(transection!=null) 
    { 
     int id = 13; 
     StudentDtos student = session.get(StudentDtos.class, id); 
     System.out.println("Info : "+student.toString()); 
     if(student!=null) 
     { 
      session.delete(student); 
      flage = true; 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (HibernateException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   } 
  catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  }finally { 
   if(flage==true) 
   { 
    transection.commit(); 
    System.out.println("Sucessfully Deleted Student Data....."); 
   } 
   else 
   { 
    transection.rollback(); 
    System.out.println("Student deletion is Failed...."); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
}

Important Note: 
SingleRowOperation(SRO) 
a. insert query 
session.save(,) 
session.persist(,) 
b. select query 
session.load(,) => if the record is not available it would return "ObjectNotFoundException". 
session.get(,)   => If the record doesnt exists, it would return null. 
c. updateQuery 
session.update(,) 
session.saveOrUpdate(,)=> first performed selection,record found, so 
latest values it updated using update query. 
=> first performed seelction,record 
not found, so perform insert operation. 
d. deleteQuery 
session.delete(,)=> Check whether record exists,only if it exists 
perform deletion. 
BulkOperation(mulitple rows) 
1. HQL/JPQL 
2. NativeSQL 
3. CriterionAPI/QBC 
save() 
* Serializable .save(Object obj) 
* This method gives instructions to save object and also return the assigned or generated identity 
value back to the application as the return value. 
* This method is own method of hibernate(not as per specification of JPA). 
note: if generators are not configure, then value assigned to id property will be 
returned as identity value. 
eg: increment,sequence,hilo,...... 
Session session = sessionFactory.openSession(); 
Transaction tx = session.beginTransaction(); 
Person person = new Person(); 
person.setName("Alice"); 
Long id = (Long) session.save(person); // Returns the 
generated identifier 
tx.commit(); 
session.close(); 
Employee.java 
@Id 
@Column(name = "eid") 
@GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY) 
private Integer empId; 
As noticed above we have told hibernated to genreate the value of empId, so 
the generated value is "AutoIncrement" 
for MySQLDB 
persist() 
*void persist(Object object) 
* return type is void, cannot return the identity value. 
* This method is given by JPA specification and it is implemented by 
Hibernate. 
* Gives instruction to hiberante to perform save operation on the object. 
* persist() doesnot allows to work with generators. 
package com.dbCurdOperations; 
import java.sql.Date; 
import java.text.SimpleDateFormat; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.StudentDtos; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class Presists { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = null; 
     Transaction transection = null; 
     boolean flag = false; 
  try { 
    session =HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
    if(session!=null) 
    { 
     transection= session.beginTransaction(); 
    } 
    if(transection!=null) 
    { 
     StudentDtos students = new StudentDtos(); 
     students.setSid(32); 
     students.setName("Munro"); 
     students.setCourse("Sales Executive"); 
     students.setCity("Wales"); 
     students.setAge(29); 
     String dojDate = "24-07-2019"; 
     SimpleDateFormat sdf = new SimpleDateFormat("dd-MM-yyyy"); 
    java.util.Date udate = sdf.parse(dojDate); 
    Date doj = new Date(udate.getTime()); 
    System.out.println("Date : "+doj); 
    students.setDoj(doj); 
    session.persist(students); 
    flag = true; 
    } 
  }  
  catch (HibernateException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  }catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  }finally 
  { 
   if(flag==true) 
   { 
    transection.commit(); 
   } 
   else 
   { 
    transection.rollback(); 
   } 
   HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
  } 
 } 
} 
Hibernate Mapping through XML File : 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import javax.annotation.processing.Generated; 
import jakarta.persistence.Column; 
import jakarta.persistence.Entity; 
import jakarta.persistence.GeneratedValue; 
import jakarta.persistence.GenerationType; 
import jakarta.persistence.Id; 
import jakarta.persistence.Table; 
@Entity 
@Table(name = "Employee_Table") 
public class Employee implements Serializable { 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 @Id 
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY) 
 private int EmpId; 
    @Column(name ="Employee_Name") 
 private String EmployeeName; 
    @Column(name ="Employee_Department") 
 private String EmployeeDepartment; 
    @Column(name ="Employee_Salary") 
 private Double EmployeeSalary; 
    @Column(name ="Employee_Company") 
    private String EmployeeCompany; 
    static 
    { 
     System.out.println("Employeee Class is Loading...."); 
    } 
    public Employee() 
    { 
     System.out.println("Zero Parmeter Constructor....."); 
    } 
 public int getEmpId() { 
  return EmpId; 
 } 
 public void setEmpId(int empId) { 
  EmpId = empId; 
 } 
 public String getEmployeeName() { 
  return EmployeeName; 
 } 
 public void setEmployeeName(String employeeName) { 
  EmployeeName = employeeName; 
 } 
 public String getEmployeeDepartment() { 
  return EmployeeDepartment; 
 } 
 public void setEmployeeDepartment(String employeeDepartment) { 
  EmployeeDepartment = employeeDepartment; 
 } 
 public Double getEmployeeSalary() { 
  return EmployeeSalary; 
 } 
 public void setEmployeeSalary(Double employeeSalary) { 
  EmployeeSalary = employeeSalary; 
 } 
 public String getEmployeeCompany() { 
  return EmployeeCompany; 
 } 
 public void setEmployeeCompany(String employeeCompany) { 
  EmployeeCompany = employeeCompany; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "Employee [EmpId=" + EmpId + ", EmployeeName=" + EmployeeName + ", EmployeeDepartment=" 
    + EmployeeDepartment + ", EmployeeSalary=" + EmployeeSalary + ", EmployeeCompany=" + 
EmployeeCompany 
    + "]"; 
 } 
}

        </id> 
        <!-- Property mappings --> 
        <property name="EmployeeName" column="Employee_Name" type="string"/> 
        <property name="EmployeeDepartment" column="Employee_Department" type="string"/> 
        <property name="EmployeeSalary" column="Employee_Salary" type="double"/> 
        <property name="EmployeeCompany" column="Employee_Company" type="string"/> 
    </class> 
</hibernate-mapping>

 </session-factory>

package com.EmployeeCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.Employee; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeInsert { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Transaction transaction = null; 
        boolean flag = false; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            if (session != null) { 
                transaction = session.beginTransaction(); 
            } 
            if (transaction != null) { 
                Employee employee = new Employee(); 
                employee.setEmployeeName("Arjun"); 
                employee.setEmployeeCompany("Kandivam Mfg Prvt Limited"); 
                employee.setEmployeeDepartment("Archery"); 
                employee.setEmployeeSalary(64445.55); 
                session.save(employee); 
                flag = true; 
            } 
        } catch (HibernateException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            if (flag) { 
                transaction.commit(); 
            } else { 
                transaction.rollback(); 
            } 
            HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
        } 
    } 
}

Inserting The Data 
Performing loading operation 
get()[best suited in standalone application] 
It perform eager loading.(hits the database and gets the record from dbtable and stores in Entity class 
object irrespective of whether we use that Object/not) if we call get(), automatically the hibernate will 
generate the sqlquery and hits the database.even if the record is not available still its the database,as a 
result of which we say get() is costly in realtime applications. 
If Record Dosent Exit:- 
package com.EmployeeCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.Employee; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeGet { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Employee employee = null; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            if (session != null) { 
               employee = session.get(Employee.class, 10); 
            } 
            if(employee!=null) 
            { 
              System.out.println(employee.toString()); 
            } 
            else 
            { 
             System.out.println 
("Record is Not avalible on this particular Id..."); 
            } 
        } catch (HibernateException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
        } 
    } 
}
