load()[best suited in webapplications]:- 
It perform lazy loading(hits the database only when we use the object data other than primaary 
keyvalue) Upong lazy loading,first hibernate creates the proxy object and sets only pk value to it.when 
we use getter methods on non-primary keyvalue then hibernate will hit the database by executing 
selectquery.if the record found then it will create a new object and injects the value to that 
object,otherwise it would result in "ObjectNotFoundException".

package com.EmployeeCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.Employee; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeLoad { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Employee employee = null; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            if (session != null) { 
               employee = session.load(Employee.class, 21); 
            } 
            if(employee!=null) 
            { 
              System.out.println(employee.toString()); 
            } 
            else 
            { 
             System.out.println("Record is Not avalible on this 
particular Id..."); 
            } 
        } catch (HibernateException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
        } 
    } 
}

session.get(Employee.class, 2);

get() 
=> It supports eager loading 
=> It won't generated proxy object 
=> returns null if record not available 
=> suitable to check wheter record available or not. 
=> Creates only object for Entity class. 
=> Best suited for standalone applications(gauranteed that loaded object will 
be used) 
load() 
=> It supports lazy loading 
=> It generates proxy object 
=> It throws ObjectNotFoundException 
=> not suitable 
=> Creates 2 object(proxy + Entity class) 
=> Best suited for webapplications(DAO-> 
Update Operation 
1.update() 
i> void update(Object object) 
This method is used to modify the record of the DBTable. 
Set the primary key value and change the other non-primary data for updation. 
To use update(), we should remember wheter record exists or not for the give 
primary key value. 
otherwise it would result in "HibernateException". 
It would directly generate "update query" without "select query". 
ii>Load the object from database and then modify 
Here we won't get Exception as the object is available we do modify the Object. 
package com.EmployeeCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.Employee; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeUpdate { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session  = null; 
  Transaction transection = null; 
  boolean flag = false; 
  Employee employe = new Employee(); 
  employe.setEmpId(1); 
  employe.setEmployeeCompany("BCCI"); 
  employe.setEmployeeName("Virat Kohli"); 
  employe.setEmployeeDepartment("Batting");; 
  employe.setEmployeeSalary(66666.6); 
  try { 
   session =  HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
   transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
   session.update(employe); 
   flag = true; 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   flag = false; 
  }finally { 
   if(flag==true) 
   { 
    transection.commit(); 
    System.out.println("Record is updated...."); 
    employe = session.load(Employee.class, 1); 
    System.out.println(employe.toString()); 
   }else 
   { 
    transection.rollback(); 
    System.out.println("Record updatetation is Failed..."); 
   } 
    HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
  }} 
}

 }

2.saveOrUpdate() 
If the object/record is already available only then it will update the record otherwise it will 
insert/create a new record 
package com.EmployeeCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.Employee; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeSaveorUpdate { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session  = null; 
  Transaction transection = null; 
  boolean flag = false; 
  Employee employe = null; 
  int ID = 4; 
  try { 
   session =  HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
      employe = session.get(Employee.class, ID); 
   if(employe !=null) 
   { 
    System.out.println("Record Before update...."); 
    System.out.println(employe.toString()); 
    employe.setEmployeeCompany("RCB"); 
    employe.setEmployeeName("Rajat Patidhar"); 
    employe.setEmployeeDepartment("Batting");; 
    employe.setEmployeeSalary(7777.6); 
    transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
    session.saveOrUpdate(employe); 
    flag = true; 
   } 
   else if(employe==null) 
   { 
    employe = new Employee(); 
    employe.setEmployeeCompany("RCB"); 
    employe.setEmployeeName("Rajat Patidhar"); 
    employe.setEmployeeDepartment("Batting");; 
    employe.setEmployeeSalary(7777.6); 
    transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
    session.saveOrUpdate(employe); 
    flag = true; 
   } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   flag = false; 
  }finally { 
   if(flag==true) 
   { 
    transection.commit(); 
    System.out.println("Record is updated...."); 
    System.out.println(employe.toString()); 
   }else 
   { 
    transection.rollback(); 
    System.out.println("Record updatetation is Failed..."); 
   } 
    HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
  } 
 } 
}

3. merge() 
On the loaded object, if we want to update the data then we need to go for merge() 
package com.EmployeeCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.Employee; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeMerge { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Transaction transaction = null; 
        Employee employe = null; 
        Employee employe1 = null; 
        Employee employe2 = null; 
        boolean flag = false; 
        int ID = 1; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            transaction = session.beginTransaction(); // Start transaction first 
            // Fetch the existing employee 
            employe = session.get(Employee.class, ID); 
            if (employe == null) { 
                System.out.println("No employee found with ID: " + ID); 
                return; 
            } 
            // Create a new employee object with updated details 
            employe1 = new Employee(); 
            employe1.setEmpId(ID); 
            employe1.setEmployeeName("Kohli"); 
            employe1.setEmployeeSalary(7777.6); 
            employe1.setEmployeeCompany("RCB"); 
            employe1.setEmployeeDepartment("Batting"); 
            // Merge the updated employee into the session 
            employe2 = (Employee) session.merge(employe1); 
            flag = true; // Mark success 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
            flag = false; 
        } finally { 
            if (flag && transaction != null) { 
                transaction.commit(); 
                System.out.println("Record is updated...."); 
                System.out.println("Original: " + employe.toString()); 
                System.out.println("Detached: " + employe1.toString()); 
                System.out.println("Merged: " + employe2.toString()); 
                System.out.println(employe.hashCode() + " : " + employe1.hashCode() + " : " + 
employe2.hashCode()); 
            } else if (transaction != null) { 
                transaction.rollback(); 
                System.out.println("Record update failed..."); 
            } 
            HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
        } 
    } 
}

EmployeeDepartment=Batting, EmployeeSalary=7777.6, 
EmployeeCompany=RCB] 
Merged: Employee [EmpId=1, EmployeeName=Kohli, 
EmployeeDepartment=Batting, EmployeeSalary=7777.6, 
EmployeeCompany=RCB]

package com.EmployeeCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.Employee; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeRefreshDemo { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        int ID = 1; 
        try { 
            // Get a session from HibernateUtil 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            // Step 1: Fetch an employee from the database 
            Employee employee = session.get(Employee.class, ID); 
            if (employee == null) { 
                System.out.println("No employee found with ID: " + ID); 
                return; 
            } 
            // Step 2: Display the initial state of the employee 
            System.out.println("Initial state: " + employee); 
            // Simulate a delay to allow external updates 
            Thread.sleep(30000); 
            System.out.println("Assuming database was updated externally..."); 
            // Step 3: Use refresh() to sync the object with the latest database state 
            session.refresh(employee); 
            // Step 4: Display the refreshed state 
            System.out.println("Refreshed state: " + employee); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            if (session != null) { 
                HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

Deleting object: 
=> It refers to deleting the record  
represented by the Entity class Object. 
=> Delete the record based on the id  
value of the given entity object. 
=> public void delete(Object obj) 
Approach-1: 
session.delete(Object obj) 
directly we are trying to delete the object, so not a good approach 
Approach-2: 
First load the object, if found only then delete the object. 
refer: HBDeleteOperation 
How can u show that synchronization would exists b/w EntityObject to DBTable row? 
refer: HBSynchronizationOperation 
persistence operations 
insert=======> save(obj)/persist(obj) 
read =======> get(obj,pk)/load(obj,pk) 
update======> saveOrUpdate()/update()/merge() 
delete ======> delete(obj) 
s   
package com.EmployeeCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.Employee; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeDelete { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = null; 
  Transaction transection = null; 
  boolean flag = false; 
  Employee employe = null; 
  int ID = 5; 
  try { 
   session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
   employe = new Employee(); 
   employe.setEmpId(ID); 
   transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
   session.delete(employe); 
   flag = true; 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   flag = false; 
  } finally { 
   if (flag == true) { 
    transection.commit(); 
    System.out.println("Record is Deleted...."); 
    System.out.println(employe.toString()); 
   } else { 
    transection.rollback(); 
    System.out.println("Record Deletation is Failed..."); 
   } 
   HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
  } 
 } 
}

package com.EmployeeCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.Employee; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeDeleteApproach2 { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Transaction transection = null; 
        boolean flag = false; 
        Employee employe = null; 
        int ID = 10; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            employe = session.get(Employee.class, ID); 
            transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
            if (employe != null) { 
                System.out.println("Record Before update...."); 
                System.out.println(employe.toString()); 
                session.delete(employe); 
                flag = true; 
            } else { 
                System.out.println("Record Dosent Exits"); 
                System.exit(0); 
            } 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
            flag = false; 
        } finally { 
            if (flag == true) { 
                transection.commit(); 
                System.out.println("Record is Deleted...."); 
                System.out.println("Record Check : " + employe.toString()); 
            } else { 
                transection.rollback(); 
                System.out.println("Record Deletation is Failed..."); 
            } 
            HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
        } 
    } 
}

Generators in hibernate 
MySQL => primary key value where the generation of these values are made 
automatic. 
While creating a table, we can inform hibernate to create a columns with primary 
key value using @Id. 
It is also possible to set the values to these primary key columns using Generators 
in hibernate. 
There are 3 types of generators in hibernate 
a. Hibernate supplied generators 
b. JPA generators 
c. Custom generators 
1. Hibernate-Supplied Generators 
Hibernate provides several built-in strategies to generate primary key values: 
IDENTITY - Uses the database's AUTO_INCREMENT feature (e.g., MySQL, PostgreSQL). 
SEQUENCE - Uses a database sequence to generate primary key values (mostly for Oracle, PostgreSQL). 
TABLE - Uses a special table in the database to generate primary key values. 
AUTO - Hibernate automatically picks the best strategy based on the database. 
Hibernate supplied generators 
a. assigned 
b. increment 
c. identity 
d. sequence 
e. hilo 
f. seqhilo 
g. native 
h. foreign 
i. select 
j. uuid 
h. guid 
Assigned 
If we use this algorithm then explicitly we need to specify the primary key 
value to the table. 
assigned => org.hibernate.id.Assigned 
It works with all databases as we need to give the primary key value. 
@Id 
@Column(name = "eid") 
@GenericGenerator(name="gen1",strategy = "assigned") 
@GeneratedValue(generator = "gen1") 
private Integer empId; 
Increment 
It uses max(value) + 1 to generate the primary key value which is of int type, Works with all Database.If dbTable is 
empty it will generate 1 as the identity value. increment => org.hibernate.id.IncrementGenerator 
@Id 
@Column(name = "eid") 
@GenericGenerator(name="gen1",strategy = "increment") 
@GeneratedValue(generator = "gen1") 
private Integer empId; 
identity 
Generates the value which are of type int,long,short. This generator can be used only in such databases that 
supports "identity" 
columns. This generator works for MySQL,DB2,SQlServer,..it wont work in Oracle,PostgreSQL.... 
MySQL=> AutoIncrement feature 
@Id 
@GenericGenerator(name = "gen1", strategy = "identity") 
@GeneratedValue(generator = "gen1") 
private Integer empId; 
1.2 Using SEQUENCE (For PostgreSQL, Oracle)  
@Entity  
@SequenceGenerator(name = "product_seq", 
sequenceName = "product_sequence", allocationSize 
= 1) 
 public class Product {  
 @Id @GeneratedValue(strategy = 
 GenerationType.SEQUENCE, generator = 
 "product_seq")  
 private Long id; private String name; 
 } 
JPA generators 
These are given by Sun MS JPA specification 
It will work with all ORM Frameworks 
4 generators are given 
a. Identity 
b. sequence 
c. table 
d. auto 
identity 
It works with MySQL database. 
It is similar to AutoIncrement feature of primary key column. 
@Id 
@Column(name = "eid") 
@GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY) 
private Integer empId; 
auto 
It works with all database 
Depending upon the db engine platform, automatically 
hibernate will use 
hiberanate_sequence algorithm to generate the 
primary key value. 
@Id 
@Column(name = "eid") 
@GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.AUTO) 
private Integer empId; 
 @EmbeddedId and @Embeddable in Hibernate (JPA) 
In Hibernate (JPA), @EmbeddedId and @Embeddable are used to create composite primary keys (i.e., 
when a table requires multiple columns to act as a primary key instead of a single column). 
1. Understanding @EmbeddedId and @Embeddable 
@EmbeddedId: Used in an entity class to indicate that the primary key is a composite key. 
@Embeddable: Used in a separate class that defines the composite key structure. 
�
� Why use @EmbeddedId? 
Helps maintain better readability and separation of concerns. 
Makes queries easier when dealing with multi-column primary keys. 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import jakarta.persistence.Column; 
import jakarta.persistence.Embeddable; 
@Embeddable 
public class ProjectInfo implements Serializable 
{ 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 @Column(name ="Project_Id") 
 private Integer pid; 
 @Column(name = "Program_Id") 
 private Integer programId; 
 public Integer getPid() { 
  return pid; 
 } 
 public void setPid(Integer pid) { 
  this.pid = pid; 
 } 
 public Integer getProjectId() { 
  return programId; 
 } 
 public void setProjectId(Integer projectId) { 
  this.programId = projectId; 
 } 
 public ProjectInfo(){} 
 public ProjectInfo(Integer pid, Integer projectId) { 
  this.pid = pid; 
  this.programId = projectId; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "ProgrammerInfo [pid=" + pid + ", projectId=" + programId + "]"; 
 } 
}

Date Mapping in Hibernate (JPA) 
In Hibernate (JPA), you can map Date and Time fields to database columns using @Temporal, LocalDate, LocalDateTime, 
and LocalTime. Hibernate automatically maps Java Date and Time types to the corresponding SQL types (DATE, TIME, 
TIMESTAMP). 
1. Mapping Java Date Using @Temporal (For Java 7 & Java 8) 
If you are using java.util.Date or java.util.Calendar, you need to use the @Temporal annotation to specify the SQL type. 
Example: Using java.util.Date with @Temporal 
    @Temporal(TemporalType.DATE) // Maps to SQL DATE (YYYY-MM-DD) 
    private Date birthDate; 
    @Temporal(TemporalType.TIME) // Maps to SQL TIME (HH:MM:SS) 
    private Date loginTime; 
    @Temporal(TemporalType.TIMESTAMP) // Maps to SQL TIMESTAMP (YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS) 
    private Date createdAt;

DB: 
Versioning or ObjectVersioning: 
It keeps track of how many times object/record is loaded and modified using hibernate. 
It generates a special column of type numeric based special number property of Entity class to keep 
track of the modification. 
This special property/col initial value is 0 and it is incrmented by 1 for every modification. 
To configure this speical property we need to use one annotation called "@Version". 
refer:HBVersioning 
�
� Versioning / Object Versioning in Hibernate 
Versioning in Hibernate helps with optimistic locking. This means that Hibernate ensures no two 
transactions overwrite each other's data without knowing it.It uses a @Version field (usually int, long, 
or Timestamp) to track changes to an entity. 
�
� Why Versioning? 
Imagine two users editing the same record: 
User A loads a product record. 
User B also loads the same record. 
User B updates and saves it. 
Then User A tries to update using stale data... ❌ This should be prevented! 
Hibernate's versioning makes sure that if the record was changed by another transaction, your update 
will fail safely. 
✅ How it Works Internally 
A version field is checked during UPDATE. 
If the current version in the DB doesn't match the entity's version, Hibernate throws 
OptimisticLockException. 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import jakarta.persistence.Column; 
import jakarta.persistence.Entity; 
import jakarta.persistence.GeneratedValue; 
import jakarta.persistence.GenerationType; 
import jakarta.persistence.Id; 
import jakarta.persistence.Table; 
import jakarta.persistence.Version; 
@Entity 
@Table(name="MobileCustomer_Info") 
public class MobileCustomer implements Serializable{ 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 @Id 
 @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY) 
 private int customerID; 
 @Column(length=30) 
 private String customerName; 
 @Column(length=40) 
 private String callerTune; 
 private long mobileNumber; 
 @Version 
 private Integer versionCount; 
 public int getCustomerID() { 
  return customerID; 
 } 
 public void setCustomerID(int customerID) { 
  this.customerID = customerID; 
 } 
 public String getCustomerName() { 
  return customerName; 
 } 
 public void setCustomerName(String customerName) { 
  this.customerName = customerName; 
 } 
 public String getCallerTune() { 
  return callerTune; 
 } 
 public void setCallerTune(String callerTune) { 
  this.callerTune = callerTune; 
 } 
 public long getMobileNumber() { 
  return mobileNumber; 
 } 
 public void setMobileNumber(long mobileNumber) { 
  this.mobileNumber = mobileNumber; 
 } 
 public Integer getVersionCount() { 
  return versionCount; 
 } 
 public void setVersionCount(Integer versionCount) { 
  this.versionCount = versionCount; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "MobileCustomer [customerID=" + customerID + ", customerName=" + 
customerName + ", callerTune=" 
    + callerTune + ", mobileNumber=" + mobileNumber + ", versionCount=" 
+ versionCount + "]"; 
 } 
}

package MobileCustomerInfo;

import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.MobileCustomer; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class CustomerInsert { 
 @SuppressWarnings("deprecation") 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = null; 
  Transaction transection = null; 
  Integer IDvalue = null; 
  boolean flag = false; 
  session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
  MobileCustomer customer = new MobileCustomer(); 
  customer.setCustomerName("Teja"); 
  customer.setCallerTune("SoloLeveling"); 
  customer.setMobileNumber(789456123); 
  try { 
   if(session!=null) 
   { 
    transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
    if(transection!=null) 
    { 
     IDvalue = (Integer) session.save(customer); 
     System.out.println("Generated ID value is  :: "+IDvalue); 
     flag = true; 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
   flag = false; 
  }finally { 
   if(flag) 
   { 
    transection.commit(); 
    System.out.println("Object is Saved.....!"); 
   }else 
   { 
    transection.rollback(); 
    System.out.println("Object is not Saved....!"); 
   } 
   HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
  } 
 } 
}

  MobileCustomer customer = null;

  try { 
    if(session!=null) 
    { 
     transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
     if(transection!=null) 
     { 
      customer = session.get(MobileCustomer.class, 3); 
      if(customer!=null) 
      { 
       System.out.println("Customer Info :: "+customer.toString()); 
       customer.setCallerTune("Nana ku Prema tho....BGM"); 
       flag = true; 
      } 
     } 
    } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  finally { 
   if(flag) 
   { 
    transection.commit(); 
    System.out.println("Object is Updated....."); 
    System.out.println("Customer Modified Count :

Time Stamping in Hibernate 
�
� Time Stamping in Hibernate 
Time stamping in Hibernate is the process of automatically storing the date and time when an entity 
is: 
Created (createdAt) 
Updated (updatedAt) 
Hibernate (JPA) allows us to handle this with annotations like @PrePersist and @PreUpdate, or 
using auditing features in Spring Data JPA. 
✅ Use Case 
Record when data was created or modified. 
Track changes for auditing or history logs. 
Automatically set or update date/time values. 
TimeStamping 
It allows us to keep track of Object is saved(record inserted) and object is lastly 
updated. 
eg: keeping track of when the bank accoutn opened and lastly modified 
To do this we use annotations like @CreationTimeStamp,@UpdateTimeStamp 
refer:HBTimeStamping 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import jakarta.persistence.Column; 
import jakarta.persistence.Embeddable; 
@Embeddable 
public class BankAccountUniqueId implements Serializable { 
    private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
    @Column(name = "CustomerId") 
    private String customerId; 
    @Column(name = "AccountId") 
    private long accountId; 
    public BankAccountUniqueId() { 
    } 
    public BankAccountUniqueId(String customerId, long accountId) { 
        this.customerId = customerId; 
        this.accountId = accountId; 
    } 
    // Getters and Setters 
    public String getCustomerId() { 
        return customerId; 
    } 
    public void setCustomerId(String customerId) { 
        this.customerId = customerId; 
    } 
    public long getAccountId() { 
        return accountId; 
    } 
    public void setAccountId(long accountId) { 
        this.accountId = accountId; 
    } 
    @Override 
    public String toString() { 
        return "BankAccountUniqueId [customerId=" + customerId + ", accountId=" + accountId + "]"; 
    } 
} 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import java.time.LocalDate; 
import org.hibernate.annotations.CreationTimestamp; 
import org.hibernate.annotations.UpdateTimestamp; 
import jakarta.persistence.*; 
@Entity 
public class BankAccount { 
    @EmbeddedId 
    private BankAccountUniqueId id; 
    @Column(name = "CustomerUniqueId") 
    private String customerUniqueId; 
    @Column(length = 50, name = "Account_holderName") 
    private String accountHolderName; 
    private Double balance; 
    @CreationTimestamp 
    private LocalDate openingDate; 
    @UpdateTimestamp 
    private LocalDate closingDate; 
    @Version 
    private Integer version; 
    @PrePersist 
    public void generateCustomUniqueId() { 
        if (id != null && id.getCustomerId() != null && id.getAccountId() != 0) { 
            customerUniqueId = id.getCustomerId() + "-" + id.getAccountId(); 
        } 
    } 
    // Getters and Setters 
    public BankAccountUniqueId getId() { 
        return id; 
    } 
    public void setId(BankAccountUniqueId id) { 
        this.id = id; 
    } 
    public String getCustomerUniqueId() { 
        return customerUniqueId; 
    } 
    public void setCustomerUniqueId(String customerUniqueId) { 
        this.customerUniqueId = customerUniqueId; 
    } 
    public String getAccountHolderName() { 
        return accountHolderName; 
    } 
    public void setAccountHolderName(String accountHolderName) { 
        this.accountHolderName = accountHolderName; 
    } 
    public Double getBalance() { 
        return balance; 
    } 
    public void setBalance(Double balance) { 
        this.balance = balance; 
    } 
    public LocalDate getOpeningDate() { 
        return openingDate; 
    } 
    public void setOpeningDate(LocalDate openingDate) { 
        this.openingDate = openingDate; 
    } 
    public LocalDate getClosingDate() { 
        return closingDate; 
    } 
    public void setClosingDate(LocalDate closingDate) { 
        this.closingDate = closingDate; 
    } 
    public Integer getVersion() { 
        return version; 
    } 
    public void setVersion(Integer version) { 
        this.version = version; 
    } 
    @Override 
    public String toString() { 
        return "BankAccount [id=" + id + ", customerUniqueId=" + customerUniqueId + ", accountHolderName=" 
                + accountHolderName + ", balance=" + balance + ", openingDate=" + openingDate + ", closingDate=" 
                + closingDate + ", version=" + version + "]"; 
    } 
} 
package com.TimeStamping;s 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.BankAccount; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.BankAccountUniqueId; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class BankAccountInsert { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Transaction transaction = null; 
        boolean flag = false; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            if (session != null) { 
                transaction = session.beginTransaction(); 
                if (transaction != null) { 
                    BankAccountUniqueId unid = new BankAccountUniqueId("TXT",3L); 
                    BankAccount account = new BankAccount(); 
                    account.setId(unid); 
                    account.setAccountHolderName("Mraks"); 
                    account.setBalance(12333.33); 
                    session.save(account); 
                    flag = true; 
                } 
            } 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            if (transaction != null) { 
                if (flag) { 
                    transaction.commit(); 
                    System.out.println("✅ Data Got Inserted..."); 
                } else { 
                    transaction.rollback(); 
                    System.out.println("❌ Data Insertion Failed..."); 
                } 
                HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

what this will do in Hibernate  @PrePersist 
In Hibernate (and more generally, in JPA), the @PrePersist annotation is used to mark a lifecycle callback method 
that should be executed before an entity is persisted (i.e., before an INSERT is performed in the database). 
What it does: 
When you annotate a method with @PrePersist, that method is automatically called just before the entity is saved 
for the first time. 
Example: 
java 
@Entity 
public class User { 
    @Id 
    @GeneratedValue 
    private Long id; 
    private String name; 
    private LocalDateTime createdAt; 
    @PrePersist 
    protected void onCreate() { 
        createdAt = LocalDateTime.now(); 
    } 
} 
What happens here: 
When you call entityManager.persist(user) or save via a Spring Data repository (userRepository.save(user)), before 
the SQL INSERT happens, Hibernate will call the onCreate() method. 
This sets the createdAt timestamp automatically. 
Use cases: 
Setting timestamps (e.g., createdAt) 
Initializing default values 
Logging/auditing actions 
Performing validations or transformations before saving 
✅ What is Caching in Hibernate? 
Caching is a technique used to store frequently accessed data in memory, so Hibernate 
doesn’t have to hit the database every time. 
�
� Why Use Caching? 
⚡ Improves performance 
�
� Reduces database load 
�
� Faster data access 
�
� Types of Caching in Hibernate 
Hibernate supports two levels of caching and an optional query cache: 
Hibernate Cacheing 
Caching :- 
*It is a temporoary memory that holds the data for temporary period of time. 
* Cache at client side will hold server data and uses it across the mulitple same requests to reduce 
the network trip b/w client           and server.  Hibernate supports 2 levels of Cache 
a. First Level Cache(L-1 cache/session cache/default cache) 
b. Second Level Cache(L2- cache/configurable cache) 
eg: Stockmarket trading,live game score,weather report,...... 
Note: 
session.save(obj),session.saveOrUpdate(obj),sesssion.delete(obj) methods keep the 
object in L1cache unitll tx.commit() is called. session.get() will get the object and keep it in L-1 
cache and same object will be used across mulitple session.get() method calls with same entity object 
id. Caching 
a. evict(Object obj) * it will remove particular object from L1-cache 
b. clear() -> it will remove all object present in L1-cache. 
c. In L1-cache, duplicate objects won't be available. 
refer: HBCachingApp 
After Db Update: 
package com.TimeStamping; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.BankAccount; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.BankAccountUniqueId; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class L1Cacheing { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = null; 
  Transaction transaction  = null; 
  boolean flag = false; 
  try { 
   session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
   if(session!=null) 
   { 
    transaction = session.beginTransaction(); 
    if(transaction!=null) 
    { 
     BankAccountUniqueId unid = new BankAccountUniqueId("TXT", 3L); 
     BankAccount bankaccount =  session.get(BankAccount.class, unid); 
     if(bankaccount == null) 
     { 
      System.out.println("Bank account is Not Exists...!"); 
     } 
     else 
     { 
      System.out.println("Bank account is avalible for the customer Id : "+ 
bankaccount); 
      bankaccount.setBalance(4444.44); 
      session.update(bankaccount); 
      bankaccount.setBalance(5444.44); 
      session.update(bankaccount); 
      flag = true; 
     } 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
  }finally { 
   if(flag == true) 
   { 
    transaction.commit(); 
    System.out.println("Record is updated for above Id... "); 
   }else 
   { 
    transaction.rollback(); 
    System.out.println("Record updatetion is Failed..."); 
   } 
   HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
  } 
 } 
}

package com.TimeStamping; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.BankAccount; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.BankAccountUniqueId; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class L1CacheingExp2 { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = null; 
  try { 
   session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
   if (session != null) { 
    BankAccountUniqueId unid = new BankAccountUniqueId("TXT", 3L); 
    BankAccount bankaccount = session.get(BankAccount.class, unid); 
    if (bankaccount == null) { 
     System.out.println("Bank account is Not Exists...!"); 
    } else { 
     System.out.println("Bank account 1 : " + bankaccount); 
     bankaccount = session.get(BankAccount.class, unid); 
     System.out.println("Bank account 2 : " + bankaccount); 
     session.evict(bankaccount); // it will Remove the Object from L1 Cache 
     System.out.println(); 
     System.out.println("---------------------"); 
     System.out.println(); 
     bankaccount = session.get(BankAccount.class, unid); 
     System.out.println("Bank account 3 : " + bankaccount); 
     bankaccount = session.get(BankAccount.class, unid); 
     System.out.println("Bank account 4 : " + bankaccount); 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
  } finally { 
   HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
  } 
 } 
}

L1 Caching Example 2 
2nd level cache 
This caching is associated with "SessionFactory", so we call it as "Global Cache". 
Application will start to search for entity object in the following order 
a. L1 cache of current session(if not there) 
b. L2 cache of SessionFactory object(if not there) 
c. Collect from db and keep in L2 cache and L1 cache then give it to application. 
It is a configurable cache and we can enbale or disable it. 
hibernae supports L2 cache through "EHCache". 
Hibernate Second Level Cache Example (Ehcache with EmbeddedId) 
This document explains how to configure and use Hibernate Second Level Cache (L2 Cache) with Ehcache in a Java project 
using a composite primary key (EmbeddedId). 
Step 1: Add Required Dependencies 
Ensure the following dependencies are added in your pom.xml: 
 - hibernate-core - hibernate-ehcache - javax.cache (JCache API) - ehcache 
Step 2: Annotate BankAccount and BankAccountUniqueId 
BankAccountUniqueId.java (Composite Key): 
@Embeddable 
public class BankAccountUniqueId implements Serializable { 
    private String accountType; 
    private Long accountNumber; 
    // constructors, getters, setters, hashCode(), equals() 
} 
BankAccount.java: 
@Entity 
@Cacheable 
@org.hibernate.annotations.Cache(usage = CacheConcurrencyStrategy.READ_WRITE) 
public class BankAccount { 
    @EmbeddedId 
    private BankAccountUniqueId id; 
    private String holderName; 
    private Double balance; 
    // Getters, Setters, toString 
} 
Step 3: Create ehcache.xml in src/main/resources 
<config xmlns:xsi='http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance' 
        xmlns='http://www.ehcache.org/v3' 
        xsi:schemaLocation="http://www.ehcache.org/v3 http://www.ehcache.org/schema/ehcache-core.xsd'> 
    <cache alias="com.FirstHibernateProject.BankAccount"> 
        <key-type>com.FirstHibernateProject.BankAccountUniqueId</key-type> 
        <value-type>com.FirstHibernateProject.BankAccount</value-type> 
        <resources> 
            <heap unit="entries">200</heap> 
            <offheap unit="MB">20</offheap> 
        </resources> 
        <expiry> 
            <ttl unit="minutes">10</ttl> 
        </expiry> 
    </cache> 
</config> 
Step 4: Update hibernate.cfg.xml 
Add the following configuration to your hibernate.cfg.xml to enable second-level caching: 
<property name="hibernate.cache.use_second_level_cache">true</property> 
<property name="hibernate.cache.region.factory_class">jcache</property> 
<property name="hibernate.javax.cache.provider">org.ehcache.jsr107.EhcacheCachingProvider</property> 
<property name="hibernate.javax.cache.uri">ehcache.xml</property> 
Step 5: Test L2 Cache Using L2Cacheing.java 
public class L2Cacheing { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session1 = null; 
        Session session2 = null; 
        try { 
            BankAccountUniqueId unid = new BankAccountUniqueId("TXT", 3L); 
            session1 = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            BankAccount bankaccount1 = session1.get(BankAccount.class, unid); 
            System.out.println("Session 1 Loaded: " + bankaccount1); 
            HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session1); 
            session2 = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            BankAccount bankaccount2 = session2.get(BankAccount.class, unid); 
            System.out.println("Session 2 Loaded: " + bankaccount2); 
            HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session2); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } 
    } 
} 
Expected Result 
First fetch loads data from DB. Second fetch loads data from Second Level Cache (no DB hit). 
Working with LOB's:- 
To work with LOB in hibernate we use 
@Lob 
private byte[] photo; 
@Lob 
private char[] resume; 
refer: HBLobOperation 
In Hibernate, when we want to store large objects like images or large texts 
(CLOBs/BLOBs), we use the @Lob annotation. 
BLOB = Binary Large Object → typically used for images, files, etc. 
CLOB = Character Large Object → used for long text, resumes, articles, etc. 
Entity Class:- 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import jakarta.persistence.Column; 
import jakarta.persistence.Entity; 
import jakarta.persistence.GeneratedValue; 
import jakarta.persistence.GenerationType; 
import jakarta.persistence.Id; 
import jakarta.persistence.Lob; 
@Entity 
public class BlobJobReferal { 
 @Id 
 @GeneratedValue(strategy =  GenerationType.IDENTITY) 
 private Integer id; 
 @Column(length = 30) 
 private String jrName; 
 @Lob 
 private byte[] photo; 
 @Lob 
 private char[] resume; 
 private boolean isactive; 
 public BlobJobReferal(){} 
 public BlobJobReferal(Integer id, String jrName, byte[] photo, char[] resume, boolean isactive) 
{ 
  super(); 
  this.id = id; 
  this.jrName = jrName; 
  this.photo = photo; 
  this.resume = resume; 
  this.isactive = isactive; 
 } 
 public Integer getId() { 
  return id; 
 } 
 public void setId(Integer id) { 
  this.id = id; 
 } 
 public String getJrName() { 
  return jrName; 
 } 
 public void setJrName(String jrName) { 
  this.jrName = jrName; 
 } 
 public byte[] getPhoto() { 
  return photo; 
 } 
 public void setPhoto(byte[] photo) { 
  this.photo = photo; 
 } 
 public char[] getResume() { 
  return resume; 
 } 
 public void setResume(char[] resume) { 
  this.resume = resume; 
 } 
 public boolean isIsactive() { 
  return isactive; 
 } 
 public void setIsactive(boolean isactive) { 
  this.isactive = isactive; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "BlobJobReferal [id=" + id + ", jrName=" + jrName + ", isactive=" + isactive + 
"]"; 
 } 
} 
package com.JobReferal; 
import java.io.File; 
import java.io.FileInputStream; 
import java.io.FileReader; 
import java.io.IOException; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.BlobJobReferal; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeInsert { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Transaction transaction = null; 
        boolean flag = false; 
        byte[] imgcontent = null; 
        char [] resumecontent = null; 
        BlobJobReferal jobinfo =null; 
        try(FileInputStream fis = new FileInputStream("C:\\Users\\HP\\eclipse
workspace\\FirstHibernateProject\\src\\main\\java\\Tej1.jpg")) { 
          imgcontent = new byte[(int) fis.available()]; 
          fis.read(imgcontent); 
          File file = new File("C:\\Users\\HP\\eclipse
workspace\\FirstHibernateProject\\src\\main\\java\\Jobroadmap.txt"); 
          try(FileReader fr = new FileReader(file)) 
          { 
         resumecontent = new char[(int) file.length()]; 
         fr.read(resumecontent); 
          } 
  } catch (IOException e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
        catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            if (session != null) { 
                transaction = session.beginTransaction(); 
                jobinfo = new BlobJobReferal(); 
                jobinfo.setJrName("Saskay"); 
                jobinfo.setIsactive(true); 
                jobinfo.setPhoto(imgcontent); 
                jobinfo.setResume(resumecontent); 
            } 
            if (transaction != null) { 
                Integer rowId = (Integer)session.save(jobinfo); 
                System.out.println("Object is saved with row ID : "+rowId); 
                flag = true; 
            } 
        } catch (HibernateException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            if (flag) { 
                transaction.commit(); 
                System.out.println("Object is Saved in Data Base..."); 
            } else { 
                transaction.rollback(); 
                System.out.println("Failed to Save the Object...."); 
            } 
            HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
        } 
    } 
}

package com.JobReferal; 
import java.io.FileOutputStream; 
import java.io.FileWriter; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.BlobJobReferal; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeGet { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        BlobJobReferal jobseekerInfo = null; 
        FileOutputStream fos = null; 
        FileWriter fw = null; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            if (session != null) { 
             jobseekerInfo = session.get(BlobJobReferal.class, 1); 
            } 
            if(jobseekerInfo!=null) 
            { 
             fos = new FileOutputStream("StoreInfo/Photo.jpg"); 
             fos.write(jobseekerInfo.getPhoto()); 
             fw =  new FileWriter("StoreInfo/jobresume.txt"); 
             fw.write(jobseekerInfo.getResume()); 
             fos.flush(); 
             fw.flush(); 
             System.out.println("Data Got Stored for "+ jobseekerInfo); 
            } 
            else 
            { 
             System.out.println("Record is Not avalible on this particular Id..."); 
            } 
        } catch (HibernateException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
        } 
    } 
}

Customgenerator:- 
Hibernate and JPA had supplied predefined genearator to create primary key value 
for almost all databases. 
eg: identity,increment,auto,sequence,..... 
if we want a primary key value to be generated for our columns as per our application needs then we need 
to go customgenerators.To create our own generator we need to implement an interface called 
"IdentifierGenerator" It is a functional interface which contains only one method public Serializable 
generate(SharedSessionContractImplementor 
session,Object object) throws HBE 
<id name="empId" type="java.lang.Integer" column="eid" > 
<generator class="in.ineuron.generator.RandomGenerator"/> 
</id> 
refer: HBCustomGeneratorApp 
Genearate unique value for student id of iNeuron in the following style 
INEURON0101,INEURON00102,INEURON00103,....

package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import jakarta.persistence.Column; 
import jakarta.persistence.Entity; 
import jakarta.persistence.Id; 
import jakarta.persistence.Table; 
@Entity 
@Table(name = "Employee_Table") 
public class Employee implements Serializable { 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 @Id 
 private int EmpId; 
    @Column(name ="Employee_Name") 
 private String EmployeeName; 
    @Column(name ="Employee_Department") 
 private String EmployeeDepartment; 
    @Column(name ="Employee_Salary") 
 private Double EmployeeSalary; 
    @Column(name ="Employee_Company") 
    private String EmployeeCompany; 
    static 
    { 
     System.out.println("Employeee Class is Loading...."); 
    } 
    public Employee() 
    { 
     System.out.println("Zero Parmeter Constructor....."); 
    } 
 public int getEmpId() { 
  return EmpId; 
 } 
 public void setEmpId(int empId) { 
  EmpId = empId; 
 } 
 public String getEmployeeName() { 
  return EmployeeName; 
 } 
 public void setEmployeeName(String employeeName) { 
  EmployeeName = employeeName; 
 } 
 public String getEmployeeDepartment() { 
  return EmployeeDepartment; 
 } 
 public void setEmployeeDepartment(String employeeDepartment) { 
  EmployeeDepartment = employeeDepartment; 
 } 
 public Double getEmployeeSalary() { 
  return EmployeeSalary; 
 } 
 public void setEmployeeSalary(Double employeeSalary) { 
  EmployeeSalary = employeeSalary; 
 } 
 public String getEmployeeCompany() { 
  return EmployeeCompany; 
 } 
 public void setEmployeeCompany(String employeeCompany) { 
  EmployeeCompany = employeeCompany; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "Employee [EmpId=" + EmpId + ", EmployeeName=" + EmployeeName + ", 
EmployeeDepartment=" 
    + EmployeeDepartment + ", EmployeeSalary=" + EmployeeSalary + ", 
EmployeeCompany=" + EmployeeCompany 
    + "]"; 
 } 
}

package com.EmpCustomGenerator; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import java.util.Random; 
import org.hibernate.engine.spi.SharedSessionContractImplementor; 
import org.hibernate.id.IdentifierGenerator; 
public class RandomGenerator implements IdentifierGenerator { 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 static { 
        System.out.println("RandomGenerator.Class file is Loading....!"); 
    } 
    public RandomGenerator() { 
        System.out.println("RandomGenerator Object is Created...!"); 
    } 
    @Override 
    public Serializable generate(SharedSessionContractImplementor session, Object object) { 
        System.out.println("RandomGenerator.generate()"); 
        int idvalue = new Random().nextInt(1000); // Generates ID between 0 and 9999 
        return idvalue; 
    } 
}

package com.EmployeeCurdOperations; 
import org.hibernate.HibernateException; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.Employee; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class EmployeeInsert { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Transaction transaction = null; 
        boolean flag = false; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            if (session != null) { 
                transaction = session.beginTransaction(); 
            } 
            if (transaction != null) { 
                Employee employee = new Employee(); 
                employee.setEmployeeName("Arjun"); 
                employee.setEmployeeCompany("Kandivam Mfg Prvt Limited"); 
                employee.setEmployeeDepartment("Archery"); 
                employee.setEmployeeSalary(64445.55); 
                session.save(employee); 
                flag = true; 
            } 
        } catch (HibernateException e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            if (flag) { 
                transaction.commit(); 
            } else { 
                transaction.rollback(); 
            } 
            HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
        } 
    } 
}

package com.EmpCustomGenerator; 
import java.io.Serializable; 
import java.util.Random; 
import org.hibernate.engine.spi.SharedSessionContractImplementor; 
import org.hibernate.id.IdentifierGenerator; 
public class PlayerRandomGenerator implements IdentifierGenerator { 
 private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L; 
 static { 
        System.out.println("RandomGenerator.Class file is Loading....!"); 
    } 
    public PlayerRandomGenerator() { 
        System.out.println("RandomGenerator Object is Created...!"); 
    } 
    @Override 
    public Serializable generate(SharedSessionContractImplementor session, 
Object object) { 
        System.out.println("RandomGenerator.generate()"); 
        int idvalue = new Random().nextInt(1000);  
  // Generates ID between 0 and 9999 
        String fanId = "RCB - "+idvalue; 
        return fanId; 
    } 
} 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import org.hibernate.annotations.GenericGenerator; 
import jakarta.persistence.Column; 
import jakarta.persistence.Entity; 
import jakarta.persistence.GeneratedValue; 
import jakarta.persistence.Id; 
import jakarta.persistence.Table; 
@Entity 
@Table(name ="Players_Info") 
public class Player { 
 @SuppressWarnings("deprecation") 
 @Id 
 @GeneratedValue(generator = "ply_random_gen") 
 @GenericGenerator(name = "ply_random_gen", strategy = 
"com.EmpCustomGenerator.PlayerRandomGenerator") 
 private String playerId; 
 @Column(length = 30) 
 private String player_Name; 
 private Double salary; 
 @Column(length = 20) 
 private String franchase; 
 public String getPlayerId() { 
  return playerId; 
 } 
 public void setPlayerId(String playerId) { 
  this.playerId = playerId; 
 } 
 public String getPlayer_Name() { 
  return player_Name; 
 } 
 public void setPlayer_Name(String player_Name) { 
  this.player_Name = player_Name; 
 } 
 public Double getSalary() { 
  return salary; 
 } 
 public void setSalary(Double salary) { 
  this.salary = salary; 
 } 
 public String getFranchase() { 
  return franchase; 
 } 
 public void setFranchase(String franchase) { 
  this.franchase = franchase; 
 } 
 @Override 
 public String toString() { 
  return "Player [playerId=" + playerId + ", player_Name=" + 
player_Name + ", salary=" + salary + ", franchase=" 
    + franchase + "]"; 
 } 
}

Connection pooling 
* SessionFactory object holds jdb connection pool having set of ready made jdbc connection objects and uses them in the creation 
of HB session objects. 
* By default hibernate uses built in jdbc connection pool which is not suitable for production environment because of performance 
issue. 
* To control hibernate build in jdbc connection pool we write the following property in hibernate.cfg.xml 
<property name="hibernate.connection.pool_size">25</property> 
Which jdbcconnection pool is best with hibernate integration? 
standalone mode -> Don't use hibernate built in jdbc connection pool use Third party supplied jdbcconnection pool like 
hikaricp(best in 
market),proxool,viboor,agroal,c3po... 
webapplication mode-> Don't use 3rd party supplied only, use underlying server provided connection pool from servers like 
weblogic,tomcat,wildfly,....

Note: DataSource(I)---------> jars provider should implement and give the class. 
Why are we not configuring the Datasource class directly in hibernate? why are configuring 
connection provider class name? 
Answer. hibernate f/w is designed to pickup the datasource class based on the connection provider 
that we have configured.by configuring in this style, we can restrict datasource and jdbc connection 
pool associated with hibernate. 
hibernate will give support only for few thirdparty vendors like 
a. hikaricp(best) b. c3po c.proxool d. viboor e.agroal 
BulkOperation:- 
* To select or manipulate one or more record/object having our choice criterial value we need to go for "Bulk operation". 
a. HQL. 
b. Native SQL. 
c. Criterian API. 
HQL:- 
1. HQL stands for Hibernate Query Language. 
2. It uses Objects based Query Language(these queries will be written based on the 
entity class names and properties name) 
3. Hibernate dialect internally converts HQL queries to DB specific SQL Queries. 
4. HQL queries are DBIndependent and they supports portability. 
5. HQL supports both select and non-select operation 
6. HQL can also be used to perform SingleRowOperation(SRO) and also for bulk 
operation having our choice conditions/ 
criteria. 
7. HQL supports positional params(?)(supported only in older versions) and also it 
supports named params(=:name) 
8. HQL keywords are not case sensitive,but entity class names and properties names 
are case sensitive. 
9. HQL supports relational operators, conditional statements, joins,aggregate 
functions, projections,.... 
eg: 
SQL> SELECT * FROM EMP WHERE EMPNO>=? AND EMPNO<=? 
HQL> FROM in.ineuron.entity.Employee WHERE eno>=? AND eno<=?(positional param) 
HQL> FROM in.ineuron.entity.Employee WHERE eno=:firstNum AND eno=:secondNum(named 
param) 
SQL> DELETE FROM EMP WHERE JOB=? 
HQL> DELETE FROM in.ineuron.entity.Employee WHERE job=? 
HQL> DELETE FROM in.ineuron.entity.Employee WHERE job=:desg 
Note: if we are selecting all columns/properties in the HQL Select query then 
placing select keyword is optional. 
HQL select Queries 
a. Entity Queries(Getting all properties values of the record) 
eg: FROM in.ineuron.entity.Employee(with or without condition) 
b. Scalar Queries(Getting specific column or specific multiple column values) 
eg: SELECT eno,ename,eaddr FROM in.ineuron.entity.Employee (with or without condition) 
SELECT eno From in.ineuron.entity.Employee(with or without condition) 
SELECT count(*) From in.ineuron.entity.Employee 
Example to get All the records from the DBTable using hibernate 
package com.HibernateBulkOperations; 
import java.util.List; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class GetHibernateBulkOperations { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session =null; 
  try { 
   session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
   if(session!=null) 
   { 
    org.hibernate.query.Query<MobilesProductsEntity> query = session.createQuery( 
         "FROM com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity " + 
         "WHERE productTitle IN (" + 
         "   SELECT productTitle " + 
         "   FROM com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity " + 
         "   WHERE offerPrice < 7000 AND offerPrice != 0" + 
         ") ORDER BY offerPrice ASC", 
         MobilesProductsEntity.class 
     ); 
    List<MobilesProductsEntity> mobilesList = query.list(); 
    mobilesList.forEach(mobile -> System.out.println(mobile.getmainDetails())); 
   } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
  finally { 
   if(session!=null) 
   { 
    HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
}

Or we Can use This 
org.hibernate.query.Query<MobilesProductsEntity> query = session.createQuery( 
         "FROM com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity " + 
         "WHERE productTitle IN (" + 
         "   SELECT productTitle " + 
         "   FROM com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity " + 
         "   WHERE offerPrice <= :id1 AND offerPrice != :id2" + 
         ") ORDER BY offerPrice ASC", 
         MobilesProductsEntity.class 
     ); 
    query.setParameter("id1", 7000); 
     query.setParameter("id2", 0); 
    List<MobilesProductsEntity> mobilesList = query.list(); 
    mobilesList.forEach(mobile -> System.out.println(mobile.getmainDetails())); 
Note: 
If we use xml approach setter and getter methods are mandatory, but if we use 
Annotations for mapping setter and getter 
methods are not required, hibernate internally uses reflection api and it binds the 
value from ResultSet to private properties 
of the Model. 
Note: 
In plain jdbc converting ResultSet object to DTO object is a manual process, where 
as in orm framework like hibernate, 
spring jdbc, spring orm and spring datajpa same happens internally using 
"rowmapper"concept. 
list() or getResultList(): 
1. It internally uses eager loading for bulk operations. 
2. It returns the collection directly. 
3. Generates only one query to get all the records. 
4. suitable for good performance. 
5. It won't generate proxy object. 
6. It is not deprecated and it is the industry standard approach. 
iterate() 
1. It internally uses lazy loading for bulk operation 
2. It returns the iterator pointing to collection object. 
3. Generates n+1 query to get all the records. 
4. Not suitable, it degrades the performance. 
5. It generates Proxy object. 
6. It is deprecated becoz of performance issue. 
Bulk operation for retreiving the record 
a. All columns ========> List<EntityType> 
b. multiple columns ====> List<Object[]> 
c. only one column ====> List<datatype of property> 
Note: To avoid null checking in our application,we can use 
JDK8 supplied api called 
"Optional". 
Employee employee = query.uniqueResult(); 
if (employee != null) 
 System.out.println(employee); 
else 
System.out.println("Record not found for the given id ::"+id); 
Optional<Employee> optional = query.uniqueResultOptional(); 
if (optional.isPresent()) { 
 Employee employee = optional.get(); 
 System.out.println(employee); 
} else{ 
 System.out.println("Record not found for the given id :: 
" + id); 
} 
Note: we should use get()/load() if we are getting record based on primary key 
value, 
we can use uniqueResult()/uniqueResultOptional() if we are getting 
record based on non-primary key value. 
refer: HibernateBulkOperation 
package com.HibernateBulkOperations; 
import java.util.List; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.query.Query; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class GetBulkOperationsCode2 { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            if (session != null) { 
                Query<Object[]> query = session.createQuery( 
                    "SELECT sid, brand, productTitle, timeStamp, offerPrice, originalPrice, 
stockAvailability " + 
                    "FROM com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity " + 
                    "WHERE productTitle IN (" + 
                    "   SELECT productTitle " + 
                    "   FROM com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity " + 
                    "   WHERE offerPrice <= :id1 AND offerPrice != :id2" + 
                    ") ORDER BY offerPrice ASC", 
                    Object[].class 
                ); 
                query.setParameter("id1", 6500); 
                query.setParameter("id2", 0); 
                List<Object[]> resultList = query.getResultList();     
                for (Object[] row : resultList) { 
                    System.out.println( 
                        "SID: " + row[0] + 
                        ", Brand: " + row[1] + 
                        ", Title: " + row[2] + 
                        ", Timestamp: " + row[3] + 
                        ", Offer Price: ₹" + row[4] + 
                        ", Original Price: ₹" + row[5] + 
                        ", Stock: " + row[6] 
                    ); 
                } 
            } 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            if (session != null) { 
                HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

package com.HibernateBulkOperations; 
import java.util.List; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.query.Query; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class UniqueColumnResult { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = null; 
  try { 
   session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
   if (session != null) { 
    // Corrected query type: Query<String> instead of raw Query 
    Query<String> query = session.createQuery( 
      "SELECT productTitle FROM 
com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity WHERE sid = :id1", 
      String.class); 
    query.setParameter("id1", 111); 
    // Use getResultList instead of list() to avoid deprecated method 
usage 
    List<String> list = query.getResultList(); 
    if (!list.isEmpty()) { 
     String title = list.get(0); 
     System.out.println("Title : " + title); 
    } else { 
     System.out.println("Record does not exist...!"); 
    } 
   } 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } finally { 
   if (session != null) { 
    HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
   } 
  } 
 } 
}

HQLInsert operation:- 
It is not possible to insert one record to the database directly using insert query,becoz linking generators with HQL 
insert query is not possible. so we use session.save() method to insert a record. 
We can use HQL insert query to insert bulk record into one db table by selecting them from another db table. 
eg: insert into .... values (query is not given) 
insert into ... SELECT FROM ...... (given to perform bulk operation) 
insurance policy (table filled with records)  
premium_insurance_policy(new table) where tenure>=25 years 
package com.HibernateBulkOperations; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import org.hibernate.query.Query; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class UpdateProduct { 
    public static void main(String[] args) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Transaction transaction = null; 
        boolean flag = false; 
        int count = 0; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            if (session != null) { 
                transaction = session.beginTransaction(); 
                Query<?> query = session.createQuery( 
                    "UPDATE com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity " + 
                    "SET offerPrice = :id1 " + 
                    "WHERE originalPrice <= :id2" 
                ); 
                query.setParameter("id1", 7777); 
                query.setParameter("id2", 9000); 
                count = query.executeUpdate(); 
                flag = true; 
            } 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
        } finally { 
            try { 
                if (transaction != null) { 
                    if (flag) { 
                        transaction.commit(); 
                        System.out.println("Number of records updated: " + count); 
                    } else { 
                        transaction.rollback(); 
                        System.out.println("No record exists to update..."); 
                    } 
                } 
            } catch (Exception e) { 
                e.printStackTrace(); 
            } 
            if (session != null) { 
                HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
                HibernateUtil.closeSessionFactory(); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

Entity Class:- 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import jakarta.persistence.*; 
@Entity 
@Table(name = "FlipKart_Premium_Mobile_Data") 
public class PremiumMobilesProductEntity { 
    @Id 
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY) 
    @Column(name = "sid", updatable = false, insertable = false) 
    private Long sid; 
    @Column(name = "brand", length = 10) 
    private String brand; 
    @Column(name = "product_Title", length = 200) 
    private String productTitle; 
    @Column(name = "offer_Price") 
    private Double offerPrice; 
    @Column(name = "original_Price") 
    private Double originalPrice; 
    @Column(name = "stock_Availability", length = 5) 
    private String stockAvailability; 
    @Column(name = "product_Rating") 
    private Double productRating; 
    // Getters & Setters 
    public Long getSid() { return sid; } 
    public void setSid(Long sid) { this.sid = sid; } 
    public String getBrand() { return brand; } 
    public void setBrand(String brand) { this.brand = brand; } 
    public String getProductTitle() { return productTitle; } 
    public void setProductTitle(String productTitle) { this.productTitle = productTitle; } 
    public Double getOfferPrice() { return offerPrice; } 
    public void setOfferPrice(Double offerPrice) { this.offerPrice = offerPrice; } 
    public Double getOriginalPrice() { return originalPrice; } 
    public void setOriginalPrice(Double originalPrice) { this.originalPrice = originalPrice; } 
    public String getStockAvailability() { return stockAvailability; } 
    public void setStockAvailability(String stockAvailability) { this.stockAvailability = 
stockAvailability; } 
    public Double getProductRating() { return productRating; } 
    public void setProductRating(Double productRating) { this.productRating = productRating; } 
    @Override 
    public String toString() { 
        return "PremiumMobilesProductEntity[" + 
               "sid=" + sid + 
               ", brand=" + brand + 
               ", productTitle=" + productTitle + 
               ", offerPrice=" + offerPrice + 
               ", originalPrice=" + originalPrice + 
               ", stockAvailability=" + stockAvailability + 
               ", productRating=" + productRating + 
               "]"; 
    } 
} 
DAO Layer:- 
package com.PremiumMobiles.Dao; 
public interface PremiumMobilesDao { 
    /** 
     * Copies all MobileProduct rows whose offerPrice >= price 
     * into the PremiumMobilesProductEntity table. Returns a message. 
     */ 
    String transferPremiumMobiles(int price); 
} 
DAO Implementation:- 
package com.PremiumMobiles.Dao; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import org.hibernate.query.Query; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class PremiumMobilesDaoImpl implements PremiumMobilesDao { 
    private static final String HQL_TRANSFER_QUERY = 
        "INSERT INTO com.FirstHibernateProject.PremiumMobilesProductEntity " + 
        "(sid,brand, productTitle, offerPrice, originalPrice, stockAvailability, productRating) " + 
        "SELECT mpe.sid, mpe.brand, mpe.productTitle, mpe.offerPrice, " + 
        "       mpe.originalPrice, mpe.stockAvailability, mpe.productRating " + 
        "FROM com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity mpe " + 
        "WHERE mpe.offerPrice >= :Price"; 
    @Override 
    public String transferPremiumMobiles(int price) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Transaction transection = null; 
        int count; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
            Query<?> query = session.createQuery(HQL_TRANSFER_QUERY); 
            query.setParameter("Price", price); 
            count = query.executeUpdate(); 
            transection.commit(); 
            return "Number of records inserted/copied: " + count; 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            if (transection != null) transection.rollback(); 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
            return "An error occurred; no records were copied."; 
        } finally { 
            if (session != null) { 
                HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
                HibernateUtil.closeSessionFactory(); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

        PremiumMobilesDao dao = new PremiumMobilesDaoImpl(); 
        String result = dao.transferPremiumMobiles(90000); 
        System.out.println(result); 
        HibernateUtil.closeSessionFactory(); 
    } 
}

DB:- 
NamedHQLQuery:- 
 So far our HQL query is specific to one session object becoz query object is created 
having hard coded HQl query on session object. 
 To make our HQL query accessible and executable through multiple session objects of 
Mulitple DAO classes or client apps we need to go for "NamedHQL" query. 
 We defined NamedHQLQuery in mapping file using <query> tag or in Entity class 
using "@NamedQuery" havinig logical name and we access and execute that HQL 
query in DAO class. 
@Entity 
@NamedQuery( 
    name = "Product.findByCategory", 
    query = "FROM Product p WHERE p.category = :category" 
) 
public class Product { 
    @Id 
    private Long id; 
    private String name; 
    private String category; 
    private Double price; 
    // Getters and setters 
} 
In Hibernate, a Named HQL Query is a predefined HQL (Hibernate 
Query Language) query that is defined using annotations or XML, 
and it can be reused multiple times throughout your application. 
This helps keep your code clean and promotes reusability. 
✅ Why Use Named HQL Queries? 
Improves code readability and maintainability. 
Centralizes HQL queries. 
Helps in refactoring. 
Queries can be cached (if needed). 
Code using Annotation 
@Entity 
@NamedQuery(name = "HQL_INSERT_TRANSFER_POLICIES", 
query = "INSERT INTO in.ineuron.model.PremiumInsurancePolicy(policyId,policyName,policyType,company,tenure) 
SELECT i.policyId,i.policyName,i.policyType,i.company,i.tenure FROM in.ineuron.model.InsurancePolicy as i WHERE 
i.tenure>=:tenure") 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import jakarta.persistence.*; 
@Entity 
@NamedQuery(name = "HQL_TRANSFER_QUERY_Premium_Mobiles", query = "INSERT INTO 
com.FirstHibernateProject.PremiumMobilesProductEntity " + 
        "(sid,brand, productTitle, offerPrice, originalPrice, stockAvailability, 
productRating) " + 
        "SELECT mpe.sid, mpe.brand, mpe.productTitle, mpe.offerPrice, " + 
        "       mpe.originalPrice, mpe.stockAvailability, mpe.productRating " + 
        "FROM com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity mpe " + 
        "WHERE mpe.offerPrice > :Price") 
@Table(name = "FlipKart_Premium_Mobile_Data") 
public class PremiumMobilesProductEntity { 
    @Id 
    @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY) 
    @Column(name = "sid", updatable = false, insertable = false) 
    private Long sid; 
    @Column(name = "brand", length = 10) 
    private String brand; 
    @Column(name = "product_Title", length = 200) 
    private String productTitle; 
    @Column(name = "offer_Price") 
    private Double offerPrice; 
    @Column(name = "original_Price") 
    private Double originalPrice; 
    @Column(name = "stock_Availability", length = 5) 
    private String stockAvailability; 
    @Column(name = "product_Rating") 
    private Double productRating; 
package com.PremiumMobiles.Dao; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import org.hibernate.query.Query; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class PremiumMobilesDaoImpl implements PremiumMobilesDao { 
//        "WHERE mpe.offerPrice > :Price"; // this is not need while using NameQuery 
    @Override 
    public String transferPremiumMobiles(int price) { 
        Session session = null; 
        Transaction transection = null; 
        int count; 
        try { 
            session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
            transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
            Query<?> query = session.getNamedQuery("HQL_TRANSFER_QUERY_Premium_Mobiles"); 
            query.setParameter("Price", price); 
            count = query.executeUpdate(); 
            transection.commit(); 
            return "Number of records inserted/copied: " + count; 
        } catch (Exception e) { 
            if (transection != null) transection.rollback(); 
            e.printStackTrace(); 
            return "An error occurred; no records were copied."; 
        } finally { 
            if (session != null) { 
                HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
                HibernateUtil.closeSessionFactory(); 
            } 
        } 
    } 
}

NativeSQL Query:- 
* It is given to execute plain SQL queries that are supported by underlying DB S/w. 
* We need to use these operations only when it is not possible through HQL 
 eg: inserting a single record. 
* It supports both select and non select operation 
* These queries performance is bit good compared to HQL because they go to sql directly without       
any conversion. 
* We write a query using table name and column names. 
package com.FirstHibernateProject; 
import jakarta.persistence.*; 
@Entity 
@NamedQuery(name = "HQL_TRANSFER_QUERY_Premium_Mobiles", query = "INSERT 
INTO com.FirstHibernateProject.PremiumMobilesProductEntity " + 
        "(sid,brand, productTitle, offerPrice, originalPrice, 
stockAvailability, productRating) " + 
        "SELECT mpe.sid, mpe.brand, mpe.productTitle, mpe.offerPrice, " + 
        "       mpe.originalPrice, mpe.stockAvailability, 
mpe.productRating " + 
        "FROM com.FirstHibernateProject.MobilesProductsEntity mpe " + 
        "WHERE mpe.offerPrice > :Price") 
@NamedNativeQuery(name ="GetProduct_info",query = "Select 
product_Title,brand,offer_Price,original_Price from 
productpricetrack.flipkart_premium_mobile_data where offer_Price <= 
:type") 
@NamedNativeQuery(name ="GetAllProducts",query = "Select * from 
productpricetrack.flipkart_premium_mobile_data",resultClass = 
PremiumMobilesProductEntity.class) 
@NamedNativeQuery(name = "DeleteProduct",query = "Delete  from 
productpricetrack.flipkart_premium_mobile_data where stock_Availability = 
:info") 
@Table(name = "FlipKart_Premium_Mobile_Data")

    @Column(name = "offer_Price") 
    private Double offerPrice; 
    @Column(name = "original_Price") 
    private Double originalPrice; 
    @Column(name = "stock_Availability", length = 5)

public class GetprodlessOf120k { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
  try { 
   NativeQuery<Object[]> query =  session.getNamedNativeQuery("GetProduct_info"); 
   query.setParameter("type", 120000); 
   List<Object[]> prodlist = query.list(); 
   prodlist.forEach(row -> 
   { 
    for (Object obj : row) { 
     System.out.print(obj+"\t <----> \t");  
    } 
    System.out.println(); 
   }); 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  } 
 } 
}

package com.PremiumMobiles.test; 
import org.hibernate.Session; 
import org.hibernate.Transaction; 
import org.hibernate.query.NativeQuery; 
import com.FirstHibernateProject.PremiumMobilesProductEntity; 
import com.HibernateUtils.HibernateUtil; 
public class DeleteProducts { 
 public static void main(String[] args) { 
  Session session = HibernateUtil.getSession(); 
  Transaction transection =null; 
  boolean flag = false; 
  int count = 0; 
  try { 
   GetallpremiumprodDetails.main(args); 
   if(!session.getTransaction().isActive()) 
   { 
    transection = session.beginTransaction(); 
   } 
   NativeQuery<PremiumMobilesProductEntity> deletequery =  
session.getNamedNativeQuery("DeleteProduct"); 
   deletequery.setParameter("info", "No"); 
   count = deletequery.executeUpdate(); 
   flag = true; 
  } catch (Exception e) { 
   e.printStackTrace(); 
  }finally 
  { 
   if(flag) 
   { 
    transection.commit(); 
    System.out.println("No of products Deleted :: "+count); 
   } 
   else 
   { 
    transection.rollback(); 
    System.out.println("No product got deleted ......!"); 
   } 
   HibernateUtil.CloseSession(session); 
   HibernateUtil.closeSessionFactory(); 
  } 
 } 
}
